Al-Quran as Source

Defining Kitab and Qur'an in Hanafi Usul
Defining Kitab and Qur'an linguistically and technically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi technical definitions of Kitab and Qur'an, distinguish their linguistic and technical meanings, and explain why the Qur'an is considered an interpretation (tafsir) of Kitab.

Core Idea
Kitab and Qur'an are technically distinct: Kitab refers to the written revelation, Qur'an to the recited revelation; Qur'an clarifies Kitab.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, precise definitions of the sources are foundational. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and technical meanings of Kitab and Qur'an, showing how the commentators refine the terms to avoid logical confusion. You will learn why the author uses 'i.e.' to prevent misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meanings
Begin with the passage's description: Kitab linguistically means 'written thing', and Qur'an linguistically means 'recitation'. Note these root meanings before the technical shift.
The linguistic sense is general; the technical sense is specific.
2
Recognize the shift to technical usage
Notice that both terms have become predominant (ghalaba) in specific contexts. In Shariah, Kitab predominantly refers to the Quran as written in mus-hafs; Qur'an predominantly refers to the specific divine speech recited on tongues.
This predominance (urf) overrides the linguistic generality.
3
Understand the logical structure of the definition
The author says 'the Book is the Qur'an...' The commentator clarifies that Qur'an is an interpretive term (tafsir) for Kitab, not that the entire phrase defines Kitab. The rest of the description defines Qur'an itself, avoiding the logical error of including the defined within the definition.
The particle 'ay' (i.e.) signals this interpretive role.
4
Refute the misunderstanding
Some imagined that Qur'an as a verbal noun could mean 'the recited' and include both divine and human speech. The passage rejects this because it contradicts established common usage (urf) and is far from understanding, even if linguistically possible.
The mashayikh do not debate this, but the correct, accepted interpretation is preferred.
5
Apply the usul perspective
Usul scholars use both Kitab and Qur'an to refer to the whole Quran or any part (e.g., a verse), because they investigate the Quran as evidence (dalil) for rulings, and evidence is often a single verse.
This part-whole usage is a practical need in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ( الرُّكُنُ الْأَوَّلُ فِي الْكِتَابِ ، وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ اسْمٌ لِلْمَكْتُوبِ غَلَبَ فِي عُرْفِ أَهْلِ الشَّرْعِ عَلَى كِتَابِ اللهِ تَعَالَى الْمُثْبَتِ فِي الْمَصَاحِفِ كَمَا غَلَبَ فِي عُرُفِ أَهْلِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ عَلَى كِتَابِ سِيبَوَيْهِ وَالْقُرْآنُ فِي اللُّغَةِ مَصْدَرٌ بِمَعْنَى الْقِرَاءَةِ غَلَبَ فِي الْعُرْفِ الْعَامِّ عَلَى الْمَجْمُوعِ الْمُعَيَّنِ مِنْ كَلَامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْمَقْرُوءِ عَلَى أَلْسِنَةِ الْعِبَادِ ، وَهُوَ فِى هَذَا الْمَعْنَى أَشْهَرُ مِنْ لَفْظِ الْكِتَابِ وَأَظْهَرُ فَلِهَذَا جُعِلَ تَفْسِيرًا لَهُ حَيْثُ قِيلَ الْكِتَابُ هُوَ الْقُرْآنُ الْمُنَزَّلُ عَلَى الرَّسُولِ الْمَكْتُوبُ فِي المَصَاحِفِ الْمَنْقُولُ إلَيْنَا نَقَلا مُتَوَاتِرًا بَلا شُبُهَةٍ عَلَى أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ هُوَ تَفْسِيرٌ لِلْكِتاب وَبَاقِي الْكَلَامِ تَعْرِيفٌ لِلْقُرْآنِ وَتَمُيِينٌ لَهُ عَمَّا يَشْتَبِهُ بِهِ لَا أَنَّ الْمَجُمُوعَ تَعْرِيفٌ لِلْكِتَابِ لِيَلْزَمَ ذِكْرُ الْمَحْدُودِ فِي الْحَدْ وَلَا أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ مَصْدَرٌ بِمَعْنَى الْمَقْرُوءِ لِيَشْمَلَ كَلَامَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَغَيْرَهُ عَلَى مَا تَوَهَّمَهُ الْبَعْضُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِلْعُرُفِ بَعِيدٌ عَنْ الفَهم ، إن كَانَ صَحِيحًا فِي اللُّغَةِ وَالْمَشَايِحُ ، وَإِنْ كَانُوا لَا يُنَاقَشُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا وَجْهَ لِحَمْلِ كَلَامِهِمْ عَلَيْهِ مَعَ ظُهُورِ الْوَجْهِ الصَّحِيحِ الْمَقْبُولِ عِندَ الْكُلِّ فَلِإِزَالَةِ هَذَا الْوَهُمِ صَرَّحَ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِحَرْفِ التَّفْسِيرِ ، وَقَالَ أَى الْقُرْآنُ ، وَهُوَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا بَيْنَ دَفَتَى الْمَصَاحِفِ تَوَاتُرًا ، ثُمَّ كُلِّ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالْقُرْآنِ يُطْلَقُ عِندَ الأُصُولِيِّينَ عَلَى الْمَجْمُوعِ وَعَلَى كُلِّ جُزْء مِنْهُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ إِنَّمَا يَبْحَثُونَ عَنْهُ مِنْ حيث إنَّهُ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ ، وَذَلِكَ آيَةً آيَةً لَا مَجْمُوعَ الْقُرْآنِ فَاحْتَاجُوا إِلَى.
His statement: 'The first pillar is the Book, which in language is a name for that which is written, but it has become predominant in the technical usage of the people of Shariah for the Book of Allah, the Exalted, established in the mus-hafs, just as it has become predominant in the usage of grammarians for the book of Sibawayh. The Qur'an in language is a verbal noun meaning recitation, but it has become predominant in general usage for the specific collection of the speech of Allah, the Exalted, recited on the tongues of servants. In this meaning it is more famous and clearer than the term 'Kitab', and therefore it was made an interpretation of it when it was said: 'The Book is the Qur'an revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-hafs, transmitted to us by mutawatir transmission without any doubt.' This is to indicate that the Qur'an is the interpretation of the Book, and the rest of the statement is a definition of the Qur'an and a distinction from what resembles it; not that the whole is a definition of the Book, which would necessitate mentioning the defined in the definition, nor that the Qur'an is a verbal noun meaning the recited thing to include the speech of Allah and others, as some have imagined. Because that is contrary to common usage and far from understanding, even if it is linguistically correct. The mashayikh, even though they do not object to that, still there is no reason to interpret their words that way when the correct and accepted interpretation is apparent to all. So to remove this misunderstanding, the author made explicit the particle of interpretation and said 'i.e., the Qur'an', and it is what has been transmitted to us between the covers of the mus-hafs mutawatir. Then each of 'Kitab' and 'Qur'an' is used by the usuliyyun for both the whole and every part of it, because they only investigate it as evidence for the ruling, and that is verse by verse, not the entire Qur'an. So they needed.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a technical definition of the first source of Islamic law: the Book (Kitab). The commentator first notes the linguistic and technical meanings. Linguistically, Kitab means 'written thing', but in Shariah it predominantly refers to the Quran as recorded in mus-hafs. Similarly, Qur'an linguistically means 'recitation', but technically it is the specific divine speech. The passage clarifies that when the author says 'the Book is the Qur'an', the Qur'an is an interpretive term for Kitab, not the entire statement being a definition of Kitab. This avoids the logical error of including the defined within the definition. The commentator also refutes the idea that Qur'an as a verbal noun could encompass both divine and human speech, insisting on the technical predominance. Finally, usul scholars use both terms to refer to the whole Quran or any part (verse) because they consider each verse as evidence. This shows the Hanafi precision in defining sources and their evidentiary scope.

Key Terms
كتاب (kitāb): In Shariah technical usage, the Quran as written in mus-hafs, transmitted mutawatir.
قرآن (qurʾān): The specific divine speech revealed to the Prophet Muhammad, recited on tongues, and transmitted mutawatir.
تفسير (tafsīr): In this context, the term 'Qur'an' is an interpretation (tafsir) of 'Kitab', meaning it explains what Kitab refers to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author use the particle of interpretation 'أي' (meaning 'i.e.') when defining Kitab?
A) To indicate that Kitab is a homonym
B) To show that the following description defines Qur'an, not Kitab directly
C) To emphasize that Kitab is written
D) To reject the mutawatir transmission

Key Takeaway
Kitab and Qur'an are both used for the Quran, but Kitab emphasizes the written form and Qur'an the recited form; the Hanafi definition is precise to avoid logical errors.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
10 min
Defining al-Kitab and al-Quran in Hanafi Usul
Definition and refinement of Kitab and Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the terms al-Kitab and al-Quran in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, distinguish the technical from linguistic meanings, and explain why the author restricts the definition to tawatur transmission in the mus-hafs.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of the Quran is precise: only what is preserved between the mus-hafs by tawatur counts.

In Hanafi usul, precise definitions are the foundation of sound legal reasoning. This passage from Al-Tawdih and its commentary clarifies exactly what we mean by 'the Book' and 'the Qur'an'—terms that might seem interchangeable but carry distinct technical nuances. We will unpack the linguistic origins, the technical shift, and the critical refinement that excludes everything that is not Quran, from other scriptures to irregular recitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meanings of Kitab and Quran
The passage starts by stating the literal meanings: Kitab means 'written thing', Quran means 'reading/recitation'. These are general linguistic origins.
Note that these are not the shari'i definitions yet.
2
Observe the customary shift (ghalabah) in Shari'ah
In the custom of Islamic scholars, 'al-Kitab' came to refer primarily to the Book of Allah; similarly, 'al-Quran' became the specific body of Allah's speech recited. This is a technical narrowing via custom.
This is analogous to the maxim: 'al-haqiqah al-shar'iyyah muqaddamah ala al-lughawiyyah'.
3
Distinguish Kitab from Quran as explanation vs defined
The author clarifies that when we say 'the Book is the Quran...', the Quran is an explanation (tafsir) of the Book, not a repetition of the defined term. This avoids circularity.
The definiendum is 'Kitab', the definiens includes 'Quran' as an explanation, not as part of the definition.
4
Identify the essential attributes in the Hanafi definition
The definition includes: (1) revealed to the Messenger, (2) written in the mus-hafs, (3) transmitted by tawatur. Different usulis include or exclude inimitability and revelation; the author (Sadr al-Shariah) restricts to tawatur transmission in the mus-hafs.
This minimalist definition is intentional: it excludes everything else without extra conditions.
5
Understand why tawatur and mus-haf alone suffice
By requiring only that the text is between the covers of the mus-hafs and transmitted by tawatur, the definition automatically excludes previous scriptures, hadith (qudsi and nabawi), abrogated recitations, and irregular qira'at—none of these meet both conditions.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle of ihtiraz (disambiguation) through precise, necessary and sufficient conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ( الرُّكُنُ الْأَوَّلُ فِي الْكِتَابِ ، وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ اسْمٌ لِلْمَكْتُوبِ غَلَبَ فِي عُرْفِ أَهْلِ الشَّرْعِ عَلَى كِتَابِ اللهِ تَعَالَى الْمُثْبَتِ فِي الْمَصَاحِفِ كَمَا غَلَبَ فِي عُرُفِ أَهْلِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ عَلَى كِتَابِ سِيبَوَيْهِ وَالْقُرْآنُ فِي اللُّغَةِ مَصْدَرٌ بِمَعْنَى الْقِرَاءَةِ غَلَبَ فِي الْعُرْفِ الْعَامِّ عَلَى الْمَجْمُوعِ الْمُعَيَّنِ مِنْ كَلَامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْمَقْرُوءِ عَلَى أَلْسِنَةِ الْعِبَادِ ، وَهُوَ فِى هَذَا الْمَعْنَى أَشْهَرُ مِنْ لَفْظِ الْكِتَابِ وَأَظْهَرُ فَلِهَذَا جُعِلَ تَفْسِيرًا لَهُ حَيْثُ قِيلَ الْكِتَابُ هُوَ الْقُرْآنُ الْمُنَزَّلُ عَلَى الرَّسُولِ الْمَكْتُوبُ فِي المَصَاحِفِ الْمَنْقُولُ إلَيْنَا نَقَلا مُتَوَاتِرًا بَلا شُبُهَةٍ عَلَى أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ هُوَ تَفْسِيرٌ لِلْكِتاب وَبَاقِي الْكَلَامِ تَعْرِيفٌ لِلْقُرْآنِ وَتَمُيِينٌ لَهُ عَمَّا يَشْتَبِهُ بِهِ لَا أَنَّ الْمَجُمُوعَ تَعْرِيفٌ لِلْكِتَابِ لِيَلْزَمَ ذِكْرُ الْمَحْدُودِ فِي الْحَدْ وَلَا أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ مَصْدَرٌ بِمَعْنَى الْمَقْرُوءِ لِيَشْمَلَ كَلَامَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَغَيْرَهُ عَلَى مَا تَوَهَّمَهُ الْبَعْضُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِلْعُرُفِ بَعِيدٌ عَنْ الفَهم ، إن كَانَ صَحِيحًا فِي اللُّغَةِ وَالْمَشَايِحُ ، وَإِنْ كَانُوا لَا يُنَاقَشُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا وَجْهَ لِحَمْلِ كَلَامِهِمْ عَلَيْهِ مَعَ ظُهُورِ الْوَجْهِ الصَّحِيحِ الْمَقْبُولِ عِندَ الْكُلِّ فَلِإِزَالَةِ هَذَا الْوَهُمِ صَرَّحَ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِحَرْفِ التَّفْسِيرِ ، وَقَالَ أَى الْقُرْآنُ ، وَهُوَ مَا نُقِلَ إِلَيْنَا بَيْنَ دَفَتَى الْمَصَاحِفِ تَوَاتُرًا ، ثُمَّ كُلِّ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالْقُرْآنِ يُطْلَقُ عِندَ الأُصُولِيِّينَ عَلَى الْمَجْمُوعِ وَعَلَى كُلِّ جُزْء مِنْهُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ إِنَّمَا يَبْحَثُونَ عَنْهُ مِنْ حيث إنَّهُ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ ، وَذَلِكَ آيَةً آيَةً لَا مَجْمُوعَ الْقُرْآنِ فَاحْتَاجُوا إِلَى تَحْصِيلِ صِفَاتٍ مُشْتَرَكَةٍ بَيْنَ الْكُلِّ وَالْجُزْءِ مُخْتَصَّةٍ بِهِمَا كَكَوْنِهِ مُعْجِرًا مُنَزَّلًا عَلَى الرَّسُولِ مَكْتُوبًا فِى الْمَصَاحِفِ مَنقُولا بِالتَّوَاتُرِ فَاعْتَبَرَ فِى تَفْسِيرِهِ بَعْضُهُمُ جَمِيعَ الصَّفَاتِ لِزِيَادَةِ التَّوْضِيح وَبَعْضُهُمُ الْإِنزَالَ وَالْإِعْجَاز ، لأن الكِتَابَةَ وَالنَّقْل لَيْسَا مِنْ الدَّوَازِمِ لِتَحَقَّقِ الْقُرْآنِ بِدُونِهِمَا فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَبَعْضُهُمُ الْكِتَابَةَ وَالْإِنْزَالَ وَالنَّقَلَ ؛ لأنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ تَعْرِيفُ الْقُرْآنِ لِمَنْ لَمْ يُشَاهِدُ الْوَحْيَ وَلَمْ يُدْرِكَ زَمَنَ النُّبُوَّةِ وَهُمْ إِنَّمَا يَعْرِفُونَهُ بِالنَّقْلِ وَالْكِتَابَةِ فِي الْمَصَاحِفِ وَلَا يَنْفَكُ عَنْهُمَا فِي زَمَانِهِمْ فَهُمَا بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْهِمُ مِنْ أَبْيَنِ اللَّوَازِمِ الْبَيِّنَةِ وَأَوْضَحِهَا دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى الْمَقْصُودِ بِخِلَافِ الْإِعْجَازِ فَإِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ اللَّوَازِمِ الْبَيِّنَةِ وَلَا الشَّامِلَةِ لِكُلّ جُزء ، إذ الْمُعْجِرُ هُوَ السُّورَةُ أَوْ مِقْدَارُهَا أَخَذَ مِنْ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِنْ مِثْلِهِ وَالْمُصَدِّفُ اقْتَصَرَ عَلَى ذِكْرِ التَّقُل فِى الْمَصَاحِفِ تَوَاتُرًا لِحُصُولِ الاحْتِرَازِ بِذَلِكَ عَنْ جَمِيعِ مَا عَذَا الْقُرْآنَ ؛ لِأَنَّ سَائِرَ الْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَغَيْرِهَا وَالأحَادِيثِ الْإِلَهِيَّةَ وَالنَّبَوِيَّةَ وَمَنسُوحَ السّلاوَةِ لَمْ يُنْقَلُ شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا بَيْنَ دَفْتَى الْمَصَاحِفِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ اسْمٌ لِهَذَا الْمَعْهُودِ الْمَعْلُومِ عِنْدَ جَمِيعِ النَّاسِ حَتَّى الصَّبْيَانِ وَالْقِرَاءَةُ الشَّاقَّةُ لَمْ تُنْقَلُ إِلَيْنَا بِطَرِيقِ التَّوَاتُرِ ، بَلْ بِطَرِيقِ الْأَحَادِ كَمَا اخْتَصَّ بِمَصْحَفِ أُبَى رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَو الشُّهَرَةِ كَمَا اخْتَصَّ بِمُصْحَفِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى ذِكْرِ الْإِنْزَالِ وَالْإِعْجَازِ وَلَا إِلَى تَأْكِيدِ التَّوَاتُرِ بِقَوْلِهِمْ بِلَا شُبُهَةٍ لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ بِدُونِهَا .
His saying: The first pillar regarding the Book. And it is in language a name for the written thing; it became prevalent in the custom of the people of Sharia for the Book of Allah Almighty that is established in the mus-hafs, just as it became prevalent in the custom of the people of Arabic for the book of Sibawayh. And Quran in language is a verbal noun meaning reading; it became prevalent in the general custom for the specific totality of the speech of Allah Almighty that is recited on the tongues of the servants. And it is in this meaning more famous than the word Kitab and more apparent, so for this reason it was made an explanation of it, where it was said: The Book is the Quran revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-hafs, transmitted to us by mutawatir transmission without any doubt. This indicates that the Quran is an explanation of the Book, and the rest of the statement is a definition of the Quran and a distinction for it from what resembles it. It is not that the totality is a definition of the Book so that mentioning the defined would be necessary in the definition, nor that the Quran is a verbal noun in the meaning of 'the recited' to include the speech of Allah Almighty and other than it, as some have imagined; because it is contrary to custom, far from understanding, even if it is correct in language. And the mashayikh, even if they do not nitpick about that, there is no way to interpret their words accordingly given the apparent correct and accepted meaning according to all. So to remove this illusion, the author explicitly stated with the letter of explanation, and said: 'i.e., the Quran, and it is what has been transmitted to us between the covers of the mus-hafs by tawatur.' Then each of the Book and the Quran is used by the usuliyyun for the whole and for every part of it; because they only investigate it insofar as it is a proof for the ruling, and that is verse by verse, not the entire Quran. So they needed to obtain common attributes between the whole and the part that are specific to both, such as it being miraculous, revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-hafs, transmitted by tawatur. So some of them considered all the attributes for more clarity, and some considered revelation and inimitability, because writing and transmission are not necessary for the existence of the Quran without them at the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him. And some considered writing, revelation, and transmission, because the purpose is to define the Quran for those who did not witness revelation and did not perceive the time of prophethood, and they only know it through transmission and writing in the mus-hafs, and it is not devoid of them in their time, so they are in relation to them among the clearest and most manifest of necessary indications to the purpose, unlike inimitability, for it is not among the clear necessary indications nor comprehensive for every part, since the miraculous is the surah or its measure, taken from His statement: 'Then bring a surah like it.' And the author restricted himself to mentioning transmission in the mus-hafs by tawatur to achieve disambiguation thereby from everything other than the Quran; because the rest of the heavenly books and others, divine and prophetic hadiths, and that whose recitation is abrogated, nothing of them has been transmitted between the covers of the mus-hafs. And irregular recitations (al-qira'at al-shadhdhah) have not been transmitted to us by tawatur, but by ahad, as was specific to the mus-haf of Ubayy (may Allah be pleased with him), or by fame (shuhrah), as was specific to the mus-haf of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). And there is no need to mention revelation and inimitability, nor to emphasize tawatur by saying 'without doubt', because the purpose is achieved without them.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a definitional analysis of the terms 'Kitab' (Book) and 'Quran' as used in usul al-fiqh. The author (Sadr al-Shariah in Al-Tawdih) initially defines the first pillar (al-rukn al-awwal) as 'the Book', explaining that linguistically it means 'written thing' but in Sharia custom it is predominant for the Book of Allah written in mus-hafs. Similarly, 'Quran' linguistically is a verbal noun meaning 'reading' but in general custom it refers to the specific body of Allah's speech recited on tongues. The Quran is more famous and apparent in this meaning, so it is used to explain the Book. The author clarifies that when one says 'the Book is the Quran revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus-hafs, transmitted by tawatur', the word 'Quran' is the explanation (tafsir) of 'Book', not a repetition of the defined term in the definition. He rejects the notion that Quran means 'the recited' in a general sense to include non-divine speech, as that would contradict custom. He states that both Kitab and Quran are used by usul scholars for the whole and for every part (e.g., one verse), because they need attributes common to both whole and part, such as being revealed, miraculous, written, and transmitted by tawatur. Different scholars chose different attributes for the definition: some included all attributes for clarity; some included only revelation and inimitability because writing and transmission were not necessary at the Prophet's time; others included writing, revelation, and transmission because later generations only know the Quran through these. Inimitability is not included by some because it is not a clear necessary attribute for every part (e.g., short verses may not be considered miraculous individually, though the challenge is for a surah). The author (Al-Talwih commentator) argues that the compiler (Sadr al-Shariah) sufficed with mentioning 'transmission in the mus-hafs by tawatur' because that alone excludes everything else: heavenly scriptures, hadith qudsi, hadith nabawi, and abrogated recitations (mansukh al-tilawa) are not preserved between the covers of mus-hafs. He further notes that irregular qira'at (like those of Ubayy and Ibn Mas'ud) are not transmitted by tawatur, so they are not part of the Quran definition. He sees no need to add 'revelation' or 'inimitability' or emphasize 'without doubt' for tawatur, as the mere fact of being in the mus-hafs with tawatur transmission achieves the purpose of disambiguation. This is a hallmark of Hanafi usul: precise, minimalist definitions that rely on observable, universally accepted characteristics (like being in the mus-haf) rather than speculative ones.

Key Terms
الْكِتَابُ (al-Kitāb): In usul al-fiqh, the specific divine revelation known as the Quran, written in mus-hafs, transmitted by tawatur.
الْقُرْآنُ (al-Qur'ān): The specific speech of Allah recited on tongues, more famous than Kitab; used for the whole or any part.
تَوَاتُر (tawātur): Transmission by a large number that precludes doubt and collusion.
الْمَصَاحِفُ (al-maṣāḥif): The physical copies (mushafs) of the Quran, compiled during the caliphate of Uthman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author (Sadr al-Shariah) restrict the definition of Quran to 'transmitted between the covers of the mus-hafs by tawatur'?
A) Because revelation and inimitability are not necessary for the definition.
B) Because this alone excludes all other scriptures, hadith, and abrogated recitations.
C) Because the Quran is only known through writing and transmission.
D) Because irregular qira'at are also transmitted by tawatur.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran is minimalist: only what is between the covers of the mus-hafs and transmitted by tawatur qualifies, which inherently excludes all other texts.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
Defining the Quran: The Hanafi Focus on Transmission and Writing
Defining Quran by attributes and discussing scholarly differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key attributes in the Hanafi definition of the Quran and explain why i'jaz is not considered a necessary attribute for every part.

Core Idea
The Quran is defined by mutawatir transmission in musahif; miraculousness applies to a sura, not every part.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text explores the definition of the Quran by examining which attributes are essential. The author discusses different scholarly views and argues that writing in the musahif and tawatur transmission are the clearest distinguishing features, while miraculousness (i'jaz) is not required for every part since the Quranic challenge targets a sura.

Guided Path
1
List the proposed attributes
Identify the four attributes mentioned: miraculous (mu'jiz), revealed (munazzal), written in musahif (maktub fi al-masahif), transmitted by tawatur (manqul bi al-tawatur).
2
Group the scholarly positions
Note that some scholars require all four attributes, some only revelation and miracle, and some writing, revelation, and transmission.
The author later argues for a narrower definition.
3
Analyze why writing and transmission are prioritized
These two attributes are clear and observable in the present time, making them effective for defining the Quran for those who did not witness revelation.
They also exclude all other texts including earlier scriptures and hadith.
4
Understand the objection to i'jaz
The miraculous nature is tied to a sura or its equivalent, not to every individual verse or letter, based on the verse 'Fa'tu bi suratin min mithlih' (Quran 2:23).
Thus i'jaz is not a necessary attribute of every part.
5
Apply the definition to exclude other texts
Irregular qira'at (shadhdhah) are not mutawatir, so not Quran; likewise, earlier scriptures and abrogated recitations are not preserved in the musahif.
The definition effectively isolates the Quran from all else.

Source Text

تَحْصِيلِ صِفَاتٍ مُشْتَرَكَةٍ بَيْنَ الْكُلِّ وَالْجُزْءِ مُخْتَصَّةٍ بِهِمَا كَكَوْنِهِ مُعْجِرًا مُنَزَّلًا عَلَى الرَّسُولِ مَكْتُوبًا فِى الْمَصَاحِفِ مَنقُولا بِالتَّوَاتُرِ فَاعْتَبَرَ فِى تَفْسِيرِهِ بَعْضُهُمُ جَمِيعَ الصَّفَاتِ لِزِيَادَةِ التَّوْضِيح وَبَعْضُهُمُ الْإِنزَالَ وَالْإِعْجَاز ، لأن الكِتَابَةَ وَالنَّقْل لَيْسَا مِنْ الدَّوَازِمِ لِتَحَقَّقِ الْقُرْآنِ بِدُونِهِمَا فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَبَعْضُهُمُ الْكِتَابَةَ وَالْإِنْزَالَ وَالنَّقَلَ ؛ لأنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ تَعْرِيفُ الْقُرْآنِ لِمَنْ لَمْ يُشَاهِدُ الْوَحْيَ وَلَمْ يُدْرِكَ زَمَنَ النُّبُوَّةِ وَهُمْ إِنَّمَا يَعْرِفُونَهُ بِالنَّقْلِ وَالْكِتَابَةِ فِي الْمَصَاحِفِ وَلَا يَنْفَكُ عَنْهُمَا فِي زَمَانِهِمْ فَهُمَا بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْهِمُ مِنْ أَبْيَنِ اللَّوَازِمِ الْبَيِّنَةِ وَأَوْضَحِهَا دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى الْمَقْصُودِ بِخِلَافِ الْإِعْجَازِ فَإِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ اللَّوَازِمِ الْبَيِّنَةِ وَلَا الشَّامِلَةِ لِكُلّ جُزء ، إذ الْمُعْجِرُ هُوَ السُّورَةُ أَوْ مِقْدَارُهَا أَخَذَ مِنْ قَوْله تَعَالَى ) فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِنْ مِثْلِهِ وَالْمُصَدِّفُ اقْتَصَرَ عَلَى ذِكْرِ التَّقُل فِى الْمَصَاحِفِ تَوَاتُرًا لِحُصُولِ الاحْتِرَازِ بِذَلِكَ عَنْ جَمِيعِ مَا عَذَا الْقُرْآنَ ؛ لِأَنَّ سَائِرَ الْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَغَيْرِهَا وَالأحَادِيثِ الْإِلَهِيَّةَ وَالنَّبَوِيَّةَ وَمَنْسُوخَ التِّلَاوَةِ لَمْ يُنْقَلُ شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا بَيْنَ دَفْتَى الْمَصَاحِفِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ اسْمٌ لِهَذَا الْمَعْهُودِ الْمَعْلُومِ عِنْدَ جَمِيعِ النَّاسِ حَتَّى الصَّبْيَانِ وَالْقِرَاءَةُ الشَّاذَّةُ لَمْ تُنْقَلُ إِلَيْنَا بِطَرِيقِ التَّوَاتُرِ ، بَلْ بِطَرِيقِ الْأَحَادِ كَمَا اخْتَصَّ بِمَصْحَفِ أُبَى رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَو الشُّهَرَةِ كَمَا اخْتَصَّ بِمُصْحَفِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى ذِكْرِ الْإِنْزَالِ وَالْإِعْجَازِ وَلَا إِلَى تَأْكِيدِ التَّوَاتُرِ بِقَوْلِهِمْ بِلَا شُبُهَةٍ لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ بِدُونِهَا .

ترجمہ: قولہ الرکن الاول فی الکتاب اور وہ لغت میں نام ہے مکتوب کا غالب ہے شریعت کے عرف میں اس کتاب اللہ پر جو ثابت ہے مصاحف میں جیسا کہ غالب ہے اہل عربیت کے عرف میں سیبویہ کی کتاب پر اور قرآن لغت میں مصدر ہے قرآت کے معنی میں غالب ہے عرف میں اس مجموعہ پر جو متعین ہے کلام میں سے پڑھا جاتا ہے بندوں کی زبانوں پر اور وہ اس معنی میں زیادہ مشہور ہے کتاب سے اور زیادہ ظاہر ہے پس اسی وجہ سے بنایا گیا ہے اس (قرآن) کو تفسیر اس کیلئے اس حیثیت سے کہ کہا جاتا ہے کتاب وہ قرآن ہے جو اتارا گیا رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم پر لکھا ہوا ہے مصاحف میں منقول ہے ہماری طرف نقل متواتر کے ساتھ بغیر کسی شبہ کے بناء کرتے ہوئے اس پر کہ بیشک قرآن تفسیر ہے کتاب کی اور باقی کلام تعریف ہے قرآن کے لئے اور تمیز ہے اس کیلئے اس سے جو اس کے وہ مشابہ ہے نہ یہ کہ بیشک مجموعہ تعریف ہے کتاب کی تا کہ لازم آئے محدود کا ذکر حد میں اور نہ یہ کہ بیشک قرآن مصدر ہے مقرر کے معنی میں تاکہ شامل ہو جائے کلام اللہ اور اس کے غیر کو جیسا کہ اس کا وہم کیا بعض نے کیونکہ یہ مخالف ہے عرف کے بعید ہے فہم سے اگر چہ صحیح ہے لغت میں اور مشائخ پر اگر چہ اس میں مناقشہ نہیں کیا جاتا مگر بیٹک کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے ان کے کلام کو محمول کرنے کی اس پر صحیح وجہ کے ظاہر ہونے کے وقت جو مقبول ہے تمام کے نزدیک پس اس و ہم کو زائل کرنے کیلئے تفریح کی مصنف نے حرف تغیر کے ساتھ اور کہا ای القرآن وہو مانقل الینا بین رفتی المصاحف تو اترا پھر کتاب اور قرآن میں سے ہر ایک کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے اصولیوں کے ہاں مجموعہ پر اور اس میں سے ہر جزو پر کیونکہ وہ بحث کرتے ہیں اس سے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ دلیل ہے حکم پر اور یہ آیت آیت ہے نہ کہ مجموعہ قرآن کا پس محتاج ہوئے وہ ایسی صفات کو حاصل کرنے کی طرف جو مشترک ہوں کل اور جز کے درمیان مختص ہوں اس کے ساتھ جیسا کہ ہونا اس کا معجز منزل علی الرسول مكتوب في المصاحف منقول بالتواتر پس اعتبار کیا اس کی تفسیر میں بعض نے جمیع صفات کا توضیح کی زیادتی کیلئے اور بعض نے اعجاز اور انزال کا کیونکہ کتابت اور نقل نہیں ہیں وہ دونوں لوازم میں سے بوجہ تحقیق ہونے قرآن کے ان دونوں کے بغیر نبی علیہ السلام کے زمانے میں اور بعض نے اعتبار کیا نے انزال اور کتابت اور نقل کا کیونکہ مقصود قرآن کی تعریف کرنا ہے اس شخص کیلئے جس نے نہیں مشاہدہ کیا وحی کا اور نہیں پایا نبی علیہ السلام کا زمانہ اور وہ جز این نیست کہ تعریف کرتے ہیں جس کی نقل اور كتابت فی المصاحف کے ساتھ اور نہیں ہے جدا وہ ( قرآن ) ان دونوں (صفتوں) سے ان کے زمانے میں نسبت کرتے ہوئے ان کی طرف لوازم بعینہ میں سے زیادہ بیان کرنے والے اور ان سے زیادہ واضح ہیں دلالت کرنے کے اعتبار سے مقصود پر بخلاف اعجاز کے کیونکہ وہ نہیں ہے لوازم بعینہ میں سے اور نہ ہی لوازم شاملہ میں سے ہر جز کیلئے کیونکہ معجزہ وہ سورۃ ہے یا سورۃ کی مقدار ہے دلیل پکڑتے ہوئے اللہ تعالی کے اس قول سے فاتو بسورۃ من مثلہ اور مصنف نے اتفاق کیا نقل فی المصاحف تو اترا کے ذکر کرنے پر بوجہ حاصل ہو جانے احتراز کے اس کے ساتھ جمیع ماعدا القرآن سے کیونکہ تمام کتب سماویہ اور ان کا غیر اور احادیث قدسیہ اور نبویہ اور منسوخ التلاوت نہیں ہے منقول ان میں سے کوئی شئی مصاحف کے دوستوں [؟] کے درمیان کیونکہ وہ نام ہے اس معہود کا جو معلوم ہے لوگوں کے ہاں حتی کہ بچوں کے ہاں اور قرآت شازہ نہیں منقول تو اتر کے طریقے پر بلکہ آحاد کے طریقے پر جیسا کہ مختص ہے ابھی کے مصحف کے ساتھ یا شہرت کے طریقے پر جیسا کہ مختص ہے ابن مسعودؓ کے مصحف کے
Acquiring attributes common between the whole and the part, specific to them, such as it being miraculous, revealed to the Messenger, written in the musahif, transmitted by tawatur. So some scholars considered all attributes in its definition for more clarity, and some considered revelation (inzal) and miraculousness (i'jaz), because writing and transmission are not necessary for the existence of the Quran without them in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And some considered writing, revelation, and transmission, because the purpose is to define the Quran for one who did not witness the revelation and did not experience the time of prophethood; they only know it through transmission and writing in the musahif, and it is not separate from them in their time. So relative to them, they are among the clearest necessary attributes and the most evident in indicating the purpose, unlike i'jaz, for it is not among the clear necessary attributes nor comprehensive for every part, since the miraculous is the sura or its extent, taken from His statement: 'Then bring a sura like it.' The author confined himself to mentioning transmission in the musahif by tawatur to achieve precaution against all other than the Quran, because all other heavenly books and others, and divine and prophetic hadiths, and abrogated in recitation, nothing of them is transmitted between the two covers of the musahif; because it is a name for this well-known entity known to all people, even children. And the irregular recitation (qira'ah shadhdhah) is not transmitted to us by tawatur, but by ahad, as it is specific to the mus'haf of Ubay (may Allah be pleased with him) or by reputation (shuhrah) as specific to the mus'haf of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). There is no need to mention revelation and miraculousness nor to emphasize tawatur by saying 'without doubt' because the purpose is achieved without them.

[Urdu translation and commentary: The first pillar concerning the Book. It is linguistically a name for what is written, prevailing in the Shariah custom to the Book of Allah established in the musahif, just as it prevails in the custom of the Arabs to the book of Sibawayh. And Quran linguistically is a verbal noun meaning recitation, prevailing in custom to the specific collection of speech recited on the tongues of the servants. It is more famous and apparent in this meaning than 'Book'. Therefore, it (Quran) is made an interpretation for it (Book) in the sense that it is said: 'Book is the Quran sent down to the Messenger, written in the musahif, transmitted to us by tawatur without doubt, building upon that the Quran is the interpretation of the Book, and the rest of the speech is the definition of the Quran and its distinction from what resembles it. Not that the collection is the definition of the Book, lest the mention of the limited in the definition be necessary, and not that the Quran is the verbal noun meaning recitation, to include both the speech of Allah and other than it as some imagined, because it contradicts custom and is far from understanding, even if correct linguistically. And the mashayikh, even if they do not object to it, but there is no reason to interpret their words in this way when the correct reason is apparent, which is accepted by all. So to remove this misunderstanding, the author used a particle of change and said: 'That is the Quran, which is transmitted to us between the two covers of the musahif.' Then both 'Book' and 'Quran' are applied by the usuliyun to the whole and to every part, because they discuss it as evidence for a ruling, and each verse is a verse, not the entire Quran. So they needed to acquire attributes common between the whole and the part, specific to them, such as it being miraculous, revealed to the Messenger, written in the musahif, transmitted by tawatur. Then some considered all attributes in its definition for more clarity, and some considered i'jaz and inzal because kitaba and naql are not among the necessary attributes for the existence of the Quran without them in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And some considered inzal, kitaba, and naql because the purpose is to define the Quran for one who did not witness the revelation and did not experience the time of prophethood; they only know it through naql and kitaba in the musahif, and it is not separate from them in their time. So relative to them, they are among the clearest necessary attributes and more evident in indicating the purpose, unlike i'jaz, because it is not among the clear necessary attributes nor comprehensive for every part, since the miraculous is the sura or the amount of a sura, taking evidence from Allah's statement: 'Then bring a sura like it.' The author confined himself to mentioning naql in the musahif by tawatur to achieve precaution against all other than the Quran, because all heavenly books and other than them, and divine and prophetic hadiths, and abrogated in recitation, nothing of them is transmitted between the two covers of the musahif? because it is a name for this well-known entity known to all people, even children. And the irregular recitation is not transmitted to us by tawatur, but by ahad, as it is specific to the mus'haf of Ubai (may Allah be pleased with him) or by reputation as specific to the mus'haf of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him).]
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a legal definition and analysis of the term 'Quran' from a Hanafi usul perspective. The author discusses which attributes are essential for defining the Quran, noting scholarly differences. Some scholars require all attributes (miraculous, revealed, written in musahif, mutawatir transmission), others only inzal and i'jaz, and others inzal, kitaba, and naql. The Hanafi position (represented by the author) favors emphasizing kitaba (writing in musahif) and naql (tawatur transmission) as the most distinctive attributes, because they are clear and comprehensive, and they effectively exclude all other texts (heavenly books, hadith, abrogated recitations) that are not preserved between the two covers of the musahif. The attribute of i'jaz is not considered a necessary attribute because it applies to a sura or its amount, not to every part (each verse is not necessarily miraculous individually). The author also notes that irregular qira'at (shadhdhah) are not transmitted by tawatur, so they are not part of the Quran. The Urdu commentary elaborates on the linguistic and customary definitions of 'Kitab' and 'Quran', explaining why the author preferred the definition focusing on transmission in musahif. It also clarifies that usul scholars apply the terms to both the whole and the parts when discussing evidence, hence the need for attributes shared by both whole and part.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-Qur'an): The specific revelation transmitted to us between the two covers of the musahif by tawatur.
المصاحف (al-masahif): The physical copies of the Quran that contain the accepted canonical text.
التواتر (al-tawatur): Transmission by such a large number that collusion on a lie is impossible.
الإعجاز (al-i'jaz): The miraculous nature of the Quran that challenges people to produce something like it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in the passage, why is the attribute of i'jaz (miraculousness) not considered a necessary attribute for every part of the Quran?
A) Because every verse is individually miraculous.
B) Because the challenge in the Quran is to produce a sura, not a single verse.
C) Because i'jaz is not mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because later scholars rejected i'jaz as an attribute.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of the Quran emphasizes transmission and writing; miraculousness applies to the sura level, not to every part.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
12 min
Linguistic and Customary Definitions of Kitab and Quran
Defining Kitab and Quran linguistically and in shari'i custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the linguistic and customary definitions of Kitab and Quran and explain why the Hanafi usul definition avoids circularity.

Core Idea
Defining Kitab as Quran is not circular because 'Quran' is taken in its linguistic sense of 'recited', not the customary sense.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, precise definitions are essential to avoid confusion. This passage from the commentary defines the terms Kitab and Quran both linguistically and in the custom of Shari'ah. It addresses a key objection: defining Kitab with Quran might seem circular because both refer to the same divine book. The commentator clarifies that 'Quran' is used in its linguistic meaning (maqru') to prevent this, thus upholding precision in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms being defined
Recognize that the passage defines 'Kitab' and 'Quran' as foundational terms in usul al-fiqh. Note that the author begins by explaining that the Quran is the explanation (tafsir) of the Kitab.
This establishes the relationship between the two terms.
2
Distinguish linguistic vs. customary definitions
Separate the linguistic meaning (lughawi) from the customary meanings (shar'i and 'urfi). Linguistically, 'Kitab' is a noun resembling an adjective; 'Quran' is a verbal noun meaning 'recited'. In shar'i custom, 'Kitab' is what is written in the mus'hafs; in common custom, 'Quran' is the well-known collection recited on tongues.
The passage also mentions the 'urfi of the Arabs where Kitab refers to Sibawayh's book.
3
Understand the attributes of the Quran in usul definitions
Analyze the different attributes scholars included in definitions: some included all (i'jaz, inzal, kitabah, naql), some only i'jaz and inzal, and some (like the author) restricted to naql (transmission) and kitabah (writing) because these are more specific and exclude other texts.
The author chose 'al-manqul bayna dafatay al-masahif' (transmitted between the covers of the mus'hafs) and tawatur.
4
Analyze the objection of circularity and the Hanafi response
Identify the objection: defining Kitab as Quran seems circular because both terms customarily refer to the same thing. Then see the response: the word 'Quran' here is used in its linguistic sense (maqru'), not the customary sense, so the definition is 'the Book is the recited (thing)', which avoids taking the defined in the limit.
This shows the careful methodology of Hanafi usul to avoid logical fallacies.
5
Summarize the practical significance
Reflect on how this definition impacts usul: it ensures that only what is transmitted by tawatur in the mus'hafs is considered Quran, excluding hadith qudsi, abrogated recitations, and irregular qira'at.
Thus, the definition has concrete implications for which texts are considered qat'i al-thubut.

فائدہ:۔ شاریخ نے اسم المکتوب کہہ کر اشارہ کر دیا کہ کتاب حقیقت میں اسم ہے مکتوب کیسا تھ تشبیہ دی گئی ہے۔ الکتاب کی تعریف ہو القرآن کے ساتھ کرنے میں اخذ الحمد وفی الحد لازم نہیں آتا وصوفى هذا المعنی:۔ اس عبارت میں سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ عام طور پر کتاب اللہ کی تعریف کی جاتی ہے ھو القرآن المنزل علی الرسول کے ساتھ تو اب لفظ کتاب کی تعریف لفظ قرآن سے کرتے ہیں حالانکہ عرف میں لفظ کتاب اور لفظ قرآن ایک ہیں دونوں کا معنی المثبت فی المصاحف ہے جب دونوں ایک چیز ہیں تو اخذ المحدود فی الحمد لازم آئیگا کیونکہ کتاب اللہ محدود ہے اور القرآن حد ہے تو جو محدود ہے وہی حد ہے عرف میں دونوں کا مفہوم جو ایک ہے۔ جواب (۱): بعض حضرات نے جواب دیا ہے کہ قرآن لغوی معنی میں مستعمل ہے یعنی مقرر کے معنی میں ہے یعنی الکتاب ھو القرآن ای المقر واس کا اطلاق کتاب اللہ پر اور غیر کتاب اللہ پر ہوتا ہے اور کتاب سے مراد خود قرآن ہے تو اخذ المحمد ودفی
It is more famous than the Book and more apparent; so for that reason this (Quran) was made an explanation of it (the Book) in the sense that it is said: the Book is the Quran that was revealed to the Messenger (peace be upon him), written in the mus'hafs, transmitted to us by mutawatir transmission without any doubt, building upon that the Quran is an explanation of the Book, and the rest of the speech is a definition of the Quran and a distinction for it from what resembles it; not that the entirety is a definition of the Book so that the mention of the limited in the limit would be necessary; nor that the Quran is a verbal noun in the meaning of the object (maqru') so that it would include the speech of Allah and other than it, as some mistakenly thought, because this is contrary to custom and far from understanding, even if it is correct in language. And the scholars, even if they do not dispute it, but there is no reason to carry their speech upon it at the time of the appearance of the correct reason which is accepted by all. So to remove this doubt, the author took a path of change and said: 'the Quran is what is transmitted to us between the covers of the mus'hafs'. Then the term 'Book' and 'Quran' each are applied in the view of the usuli scholars to the whole and to every part of it, because they discuss it as evidence for a ruling, and it is verse by verse, not the entire Quran. So they needed to acquire attributes that are common between the whole and the part and specific to it, such as it being a miracle, revealed to the Messenger, written in the mus'hafs, transmitted by tawatur. So some considered all attributes in its explanation for more detail; some considered i'jaz and inzal because writing and transmission are not among the necessary attributes due to the realized existence of the Quran without them in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him); and some considered inzal, writing, and transmission because the purpose is to define the Quran for someone who has not witnessed revelation nor reached the Prophet's time. And 'that part is not' that they define it by transmission and writing in the mus'hafs, and it is not separate from these two attributes in their time, relating them to it. These (writing and transmission) are among the necessary attributes, more explanatory and clearer in terms of indicating the intended meaning, unlike i'jaz, because it is not among the necessary attributes nor among the inclusive attributes for every part, because the miracle is a surah or the amount of a surah, taking evidence from Allah's saying: 'Then bring a surah like it'. And the author agreed on mentioning 'transmitted in the mus'hafs' and 'tawatur' to achieve avoidance of all that is other than the Quran, because all the heavenly books and other than them, and the hadith qudsi and prophetic hadith, and the abrogated recitation are not transmitted in the mus'hafs among the people, because it is a name for that well-known thing that is known among people, even children, and the irregular recitations are not transmitted by tawatur, but by ahad transmission as is specific to Ubayy's mus'haf or by widespread transmission as is specific to Ibn Mas'ud's mus'haf. So there is no need to mention inzal and i'jaz, nor to emphasize tawatur with their saying 'without doubt' because the purpose is achieved without that. 

Linguistic and customary meaning of the words Quran and Kitab.
His saying: 'The first pillar, and it is linguistic:' This is the first part of the commentary phrase. The purpose of the commentator is to explain the linguistic and customary meanings of the word Kitab and the word Quran. The summary is: linguistically, the word Kitab is among those nouns that resemble adjectives, like the word Imam is in reality a noun but it is likened to the attribute of Imammate; similarly, Ilah is in reality a noun but likened to the attribute of divinity; similarly, the word Kitab is in reality a noun but likened to the attribute of being written. And in the custom of the Shari'ah, Kitab is called what is established in the mus'hafs, i.e., what is written between the covers of the mus'haf. And in the custom of the Arabs, Kitab is used for Sibawayh's book. And the word Quran linguistically is a verbal noun in the meaning of the object, i.e., in the meaning of 'recited'. And in common custom, Quran is called the specific collection mentioned in the mus'hafs, recited on the tongues of worshipers. So the summary is that Kitab has one linguistic meaning and two meanings in custom: (1) the custom of the Shari'ah, (2) the custom of the Arabs.
Benefit: The commentator by saying 'ism al-maktub' indicated that Kitab is in reality a noun of what is written, likened to it. In defining Kitab with the Quran, taking the defined in the definition is not necessary, and in this meaning: This phrase answers a presumed question. The question summary is: Usually, the Book of Allah is defined as 'the Quran revealed to the Messenger', so here the definition of the word Kitab is done with the word Quran, while in custom the word Kitab and the word Quran are the same, both meaning 'what is established in the mus'hafs'. When both are the same thing, then taking the limited in the limit becomes necessary because the Book of Allah is the limited and the Quran is the limit, so what is limited is the same as the limit in custom of both meanings being one. Answer (1): Some scholars answered that the Quran is used here in its linguistic meaning, i.e., in the meaning of 'recited', so 'al-Kitab huwa al-Quran' meaning 'al-maqru' (the recited), and this term is applied to the Book of Allah and to other than the Book of Allah, and by 'Kitab' what is meant is the Quran itself, so taking the limited in the limit...
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is the commentary (sharh) on the first pillar (al-ruknu al-awwal) of usul al-fiqh, which deals with the definition of the Kitab (the Quran). The author begins by explaining that the Quran is the explanation (tafsir) of the Kitab, meaning that the Quran is the actual book that was revealed. The passage then addresses a critical issue: the definition of the Quran must include attributes that are specific to it and distinguish it from other divine books, hadith qudsi, and other scriptures. Various scholars differed on which attributes to include: some included all attributes (i'jaz, inzal, kitabah, naql), some only i'jaz and inzal, and some included inzal, kitabah, and naql. The author (presumably Sadr al-Shariah in Al-Tawdih) chose to restrict the definition to 'what is transmitted between the covers of the mus'hafs' (al-manqul bayna dafatay al-masahif) and by tawatur, because this excludes everything else and is more specific. The passage then discusses the linguistic and customary meanings of 'Kitab' and 'Quran'. In language, 'Kitab' is an ism that resembles an adjective; in the 'urf of shari'ah, it is what is written in the mus'hafs; in the 'urf of the Arabs, it refers to Sibawayh's book. 'Quran' in language is masdar bi ma'na maf'ul (meaning 'recited'), and in common custom it is the specific collection recited on the tongues. A key point is addressing the objection of taking the defined in the definition (akhdh al-mahdud fi al-hadd): when defining Kitab as the Quran, one might think of circularity, but the response is that 'Quran' here is used in its linguistic sense (maqru'), not the customary sense, thus avoiding the issue. This is a typical Hanafi approach to definitions in usul al-fiqh: precision to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
الکتاب (al-kitāb): In the custom of shari'ah, it refers to what is established in the mus'hafs (written copies of the Quran).
القرآن (al-qur'ān): Linguistically a verbal noun meaning 'recited'; in common custom, the specific collection mentioned in the mus'hafs recited on the tongues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author of Al-Tawdih restrict the definition of the Quran to 'what is transmitted in the mus'hafs' and 'by tawatur'?
A) To include all divine books.
B) To exclude hadith qudsi, other scriptures, and irregular recitations.
C) To emphasize the miraculous nature of the Quran.
D) To show that the Quran is not recited in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of Kitab and Quran is carefully crafted to avoid circularity by using the linguistic sense of Quran, ensuring precision in delimiting the primary source of Shari'ah.

Definitions of Kitab and Quran: Linguistic vs. Customary Meanings
Explaining linguistic/customary definitions and why usuli definitions vary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the linguistic and customary definitions of Kitab and Quran and explain why usuli definitions vary.

Core Idea
Usuli definitions include four attributes to apply to each verse; defining Kitab by Quran avoids circularity due to Quran's fame.

This lesson unpacks a key passage from a Hanafi usul commentary that defines two foundational terms: Kitab and Quran. We will explore their linguistic roots, customary usages, and why scholars of usul al-fiqh propose different definitions. The passage also resolves a subtle logical issue: if Kitab and Quran are synonymous, how can one define the other without circularity? Understanding this will sharpen your ability to handle definitional questions in usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic nuances
Recognize that Kitab is a noun resembling an adjective (like 'Imam' or 'Ilah'), and Quran is a verbal noun meaning 'recited'.
Linguistic analysis reveals the root meanings before technical usage.
2
Distinguish customary meanings
Note that Kitab has two customary meanings: in Shari'ah (what is written in the mashahif) and among Arabs (any book). Quran in general custom refers to the specific collection.
Customary definitions often diverge from linguistic ones.
3
Understand the circularity problem
If Kitab and Quran are synonymous in custom, defining Kitab as Quran would be circular (taking the limited in the limit). The passage presents two solutions.
Circular definitions are invalid in logic.
4
Evaluate the commentator's resolution
The preferred answer: Quran is more famous than Kitab, so defining the less famous by the more famous is acceptable and avoids the need for forced linguistic shifts.
Fame (shuhrah) plays a role in definitional clarity.
5
Explain variation in usuli definitions
Since rulings are derived verse by verse, attributes must apply to both the whole Quran and each individual verse. Hence four attributes (revealed, miraculous, written, mutawatir) are commonly used.
Purpose-driven definitions explain differences.

His saying: The first pillar, and it is in language. This is the first part of the commentary's expression. The commentator intends to explain the linguistic and customary meanings of the word Kitab and the word Quran. The summary is that linguistically, the word Kitab is from the category of nouns that resemble adjectives, like the word Imam: it is actually a noun but likened to the attribute of leadership; similarly, Ilah is a noun but likened to the attribute of divinity; similarly, the word Kitab is a noun but likened to the attribute of 'written'. And in the custom of Shari'ah, Kitab is called 'al-muthbat fi al-masahif' i.e., what is written in the mushaf. And in the custom of the Arabs, the word Kitab is used for the book of Sibawayh. And the word Quran linguistically is a masdar in the sense of maf'ul, i.e., in the meaning of 'maqru' (recited). And in general custom, Quran is called 'al-majmu' al-mu'ayyan al-madhkur fi al-masahif al-maqru 'ala alsinat al-ibad'. So the summary is that Kitab has one linguistic meaning and two customary meanings: (1) the custom of Shari'ah, (2) the custom of the Arabs. 
Benefit: The commentator by saying 'ism al-maktub' indicated that Kitab is actually a noun which has been likened to the written thing. 
'The definition of Kitab being with Quran does not necessitate taking the limited in the limit, and this meaning is correct.' In this expression, an answer to an implicit question is given. The question's summary is: Usually, Kitab Allah is defined as 'huwa al-Quran al-munazzal 'ala al-rasul'. So here the word Kitab is defined by the word Quran, while in custom the words Kitab and Quran are the same; both mean 'al-muthbat fi al-masahif'. When both are the same thing, then taking the limited in the limit becomes necessary because Kitab Allah is the limited and Quran is the limit; so what is limited is the same as the limit in custom; the meaning of both is one. Answer (1): Some people have answered that Quran is used in its linguistic meaning, i.e., in the meaning of 'maqru' (recited), meaning 'al-Kitab huwa al-Quran' i.e., 'al-maqru'. The application of this word is on Kitab Allah and other than Kitab Allah, but Kitab here means the Quran itself. So taking the limited in the limit does not occur because 'al-maqru' is general and not identical to the limited. 
Answer (2): The commentator rejected this answer and gave his own answer: that according to custom, the meaning of both is one, but Quran is more famous in custom than Kitab, and this Kitab is less famous. So defining Kitab with Quran is like defining an unfamiliar term with a familiar one. As for taking it in the meaning of 'maqru', it is not appropriate for several reasons: (1) In custom, Quran applies to Kitab Allah and not to anything else; if we take it in the meaning of 'maqru', it would apply to other than Kitab Allah. (2) Taking it in the meaning of 'maqru' is far from understanding because from the word Quran the mind immediately goes to Kitab Allah, not to 'maqru'. (3) When a correct justification exists, why is there need for so many efforts? 
Position: This is the second part of the commentary's expression. The commentator intends to answer an implicit question. 
Question: Why are the definitions that the usuliyun have given for the Quran different? What is the reason for the difference? 
Answer: The commentator says that according to the usuliyun, just as the word Quran applies to the entire collection (from al-Hamd to al-Nas), similarly it applies to each individual verse. Because the usuli discusses the establishment of rulings from the Quran, and this derivation is done verse by verse, not from the whole collection. Therefore, they needed attributes that apply both to each verse individually and to the whole collection. These attributes are four: (1) Being revealed to the Messenger, (2) Being a miracle, (3) Being written in the mashahif, (4) Being transmitted by tawatur. These attributes apply to the whole Quran as well as to each verse. Now some people have taken all attributes in their definition because the purpose of definition is clarity, and clarity is greater when all attributes are mentioned. Therefore, they defined Kitab Allah as 'al-mu'jiz al-munazzal 'ala al-rasul al-maktub fi al-masahif'.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the first pillar of usul al-fiqh, dealing with the definitions of two key terms: Kitab and Quran. The commentator first explains their linguistic and customary meanings. Linguistically, Kitab is a noun likened to the attribute of being written, while Quran is a verbal noun meaning 'recited'. In the custom of Shari'ah, Kitab refers to what is written in the mashahif, and in Arab custom, it can refer to any book like Sibawayh's. Quran in general custom refers to the specific collection written in the mashahif and recited by the worshippers.

A subtle issue arises: if Kitab and Quran are synonymous in custom, then defining Kitab by Quran would involve including the limited in the limit (circularity). The commentator presents two answers. The first answer suggests using the linguistic meaning of Quran as 'recited' to avoid circularity, but this is rejected because in custom Quran specifically refers to the Book of Allah, not any recited text. The commentator's preferred second answer is that Quran is more famous than Kitab, so defining the less famous (Kitab) by the more famous (Quran) is acceptable, and there is no need for forced interpretations.

Finally, the passage explains why usuli definitions of the Quran vary. Since the Quran is used to derive rulings verse by verse, scholars needed attributes that apply to each verse individually as well as to the whole collection. The four attributes (revelation, miracle, written in mashahif, tawatur) are common to both. Some scholars include all four in the definition for maximum clarity, while others may omit some. This explains the differences.

Key Terms
كتاب (kitab): In the custom of Shari'ah: what is written in the mashahif.
قرآن (quran): In general custom: the specific collection written in the mashahif and recited by the worshippers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because they need attributes that apply to each individual verse as well as the whole collection.
C) Because the Quran was revealed in parts and these attributes ensure authenticity.
D) Because the definition must be comprehensive according to the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
The definition of the Quran in usul al-fiqh includes four essential attributes to ensure applicability to each verse for deriving rulings.

Why Usuliyyun Differ in Defining the Quran
Explains why usuliyyun differ in defining the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four essential attributes of the Quran in Hanafi usul and explain why the term 'Quran' must apply to both the entire collection and individual verses.

Core Idea
Usuliyyun differ because they needed attributes covering both the whole Quran and each verse.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a key question: why do usul scholars give different definitions of the Quran? The answer lies in the unique need of usul al-fiqh: the term 'Quran' must apply to the entire collection from al-Fatiha to al-Nas, and also to each individual verse, since rulings are derived verse by verse. This requires a set of attributes that are true of both the whole and the part. The passage identifies four such attributes and illustrates how different scholars selected different combinations based on their purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the implied question
Recognize that the passage begins by posing a question: why are the definitions of the Quran different among usuliyyun?
The commentator frames this as an answer to an implied question.
2
Understand the need for dual applicability
The term Quran applies both to the whole (majmu') and to each verse (ayah). This is because usul scholars derive rulings from individual verses, not just from the whole.
This is the foundational reason for variation.
3
List the four essential attributes
The text enumerates four attributes: revealed to the Messenger, miraculous, written in the musahif, transmitted by tawatur. These attributes are true of both the whole Quran and each verse.
These are not all essential in every definition.
4
Recognize the variation in selection
Different scholars chose different subsets of these attributes depending on their definitional aim: clarity, inclusion of only essential properties, or practical distinction.
This leads to the diverse definitions.

(۴) منقول بالتواتر ہونا
تو یہ صفات جیسے مجموعہ قرآن پر صادق آتی ہیں ایسے ہی آیت آیت پر بھی صادق آتی ہیں اب بعض حضرات نے نے تعریف میں تمام صفات کا اعتبار کیا کیونکہ تعریف سے مقصود وضاحت کرتا ہے اور وضاحت تمام صفات کو ذکر کرنے میں زیادہ ہے اس لئے انہوں نے کتاب اللہ کی تعریف كى هو المعجز المنزل على الرسول المكتوب في المصاحف المنقول عنه نقلا متواترا .
اور بعض حضرات نے صرف صفت اعجاز اور صفت منزل سے تعریف کی کہ القرآن هو المعجز والمكتوب في المصاحف کیونکہ مقصود تعریف سے یہ ہے کہ اس کے لوازم بعینہ کو ذکر کر دیا جائے اور باقی قیود لوازم میں سے نہیں ہیں اس لئے کہ حضور ﷺ کے دور میں قرآن موجود تھا لیکن مکتوب فی المصاحف نہیں تھا اور نقل تو اتر کی ضرورت بھی نہیں تھی۔ اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ جو لوگ آپ ﷺ کے دور میں موجود تھے ان کیلئے تعریف کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ تو قرآن کا مشاہدہ کر رہے تھے البتہ بعد میں آنیوالے کیلئے تعریف کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے انہوں نے تین صفات کا لحاظ کیا (1) المنزل علی الرسول ہو۔ (۲) مکتوب في المصاحف ہو۔ (۳) تواتر کے ساتھ منقول ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ قیودان کے حق میں زیادہ بین ہیں اور واضح ہیں صفت اعجاز سے کیونکہ اعجاز نہ تو لوازم بعینہ میں سے ہے کیونکہ اس کو صرف علماء سمجھتے ہیں عوام نہیں سمجھتے اور نہ ہی لوازم شاملہ میں سے ہے کیونکہ یہ صرف کلام تام میں پایا جاتا ہے قرآن کے ہر ہر جزو میں نہیں پایا جاتا اور مصنف نے جو تعریف کی ہے اس میں صرف دوصفات ذکر کی ہیں کیونکہ مصنف کا مقصود قرآن کو غیر قرآن سے ممتاز کرنا تھا اور وہ ان دو صفات سے ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ المکتوب فی المصاحف سے احادیث قدسیہ و نبویہ اور دوسری کتب سماویہ خارج ہو جاتی ہیں کیونکہ یہ مکتوب فی المصاحف نہیں اور تواتر کی قید سے قراءت شازہ خارج ہو گئیں کیونکہ وہ بطریق تو اثر منقول نہیں بلکہ بطریق آحاد منقول ہیں وہ جوابی بن کعب کے مصحف کے ساتھ خاص ہیں جیسے انہوں نے قضاء رمضان کے بارے میں یوں قروات نقل کی ہے فعدة من ايام اخر متتابعات اور یا وہ بطریق شہرت منقول ہیں اور وہ حضرة ابن مسعود کے مصحح میں لکھی ہوئی ہیں جیسے کفارہ یمین کے متعلق انہوں نے نقل کیا ثلثۃ ایام متابعات یہ ہے وجہ اختلاف اصولیین کی تعریف کرنے میں۔
Statement of the reason for difference in the definitions of the usuliyyun. Hamm Kul: This is the second part of the commentary's expression; the purpose is that the commentator answers an implied question. Question: Why are the definitions of the Quran that the usuliyyun have made different? What is the reason for the difference? Answer: The commentator says that according to the usuliyyun, just as the term Quran applies to the whole, i.e. from al-Hamdulillah to al-Nas, similarly it applies to each individual verse, because the usuli discusses the establishment of rulings from the first [verse] and this derivation occurs verse by verse, not from the whole. Hence they needed attributes that apply to each verse and also to the whole. Those attributes are four: (1) revealed to the Messenger, (2) miraculous, (3) written in the musahif, (4) transmitted by tawatur. So these attributes apply to the entire Quran and also to each verse. Now some scholars considered all attributes in the definition because the purpose of definition is clarification, and clarification is greater by mentioning all attributes. Therefore they defined the Book of Allah as: 'It is the miraculous, revealed to the Messenger, written in the musahif, transmitted from him by a mutawatir transmission.' And some scholars defined it with only the attribute of miraculousness and the attribute of being revealed: 'The Quran is the miraculous and written in the musahif,' because the purpose of definition is to mention its essential properties, and the remaining restrictions are not among the essential properties, because in the time of the Prophet ﷺ the Quran existed but was not written in the musahif, and there was no need for transmission. And some scholars said that those who were present in the time of the Prophet ﷺ had no need for a definition because they were observing the Quran; but later generations needed a definition, so they considered three attributes: (1) revealed to the Messenger, (2) written in the musahif, (3) transmitted with tawatur, because these restrictions are more evident and clear for them than the attribute of miraculousness, since miraculousness is not among the essential properties (because only scholars understand it, not the common people) nor among the inclusive properties (because it is found only in complete speech, not in every part of the Quran). And the author (musannif) in his definition mentioned only two attributes because his purpose was to distinguish the Quran from other things, and that is achieved by these two attributes: 'written in the musahif' excludes hadith qudsi, hadith nabawi, and other revealed books because they are not written in the musahif; and the condition of tawatur excludes irregular readings (qira'at shadhdhah) because they are not transmitted by tawatur but by ahad. They are specific to the mushaf of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, such as his transmission regarding making up Ramadan: 'fa-iddatu min ayyamin ukhara mutatabi'at' or they are transmitted by shuhra and written in the mushaf of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, such as his transmission regarding the expiation of an oath: 'thalathatu ayyamin mutatabi'at.' This is the reason for the difference in the definitions of the usuliyyun.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that explains why usul scholars differ in their definitions of the Quran. It opens by setting up a question: why are the definitions of the Quran given by usuliyyun different? The commentator answers by noting that the usuliyyun need the term 'Quran' to apply both to the entire collection and to each individual verse, since rulings are derived verse by verse. Therefore they identified four essential attributes: (1) revealed to the Messenger, (2) miraculous (mu'jiz), (3) written in the musahif, and (4) transmitted by tawatur. The passage then explains that different scholars selected different combinations of these attributes depending on their purpose. Some included all four for maximum clarity. Others included only the attributes of being revealed and miraculous, because in the Prophet's time the Quran was not yet compiled in a mushaf and transmission was not needed as people observed it directly. A third group included three attributes (revealed, written in musahif, mutawatir) because they considered miraculousness not essential (only scholars grasp it) and not inclusive (it applies only to complete speech, not every part). The author (the writer of the matn being commented on) himself used only two attributes (written in musahif and mutawatir) because his goal was simply to distinguish the Quran from other texts: 'written in musahif' excludes hadith and other scriptures, 'mutawatir' excludes irregular readings. The passage ends with examples of irregular readings from the companions' musahif, showing the precise scope of the definition.

Key Terms
قرآن (Qur'an): The miraculous word of Allah revealed to Prophet Muhammad, written in the musahif, transmitted by tawatur.
متواتر (mutawatir): Transmitted by a large number in every generation, making certainty of authenticity.
معجز (mu'jiz): A miraculous attribute that cannot be imitated by humans.
لوازم (lawazim): Essential properties that are necessarily concomitant with the definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What core need drives the variations in definitions of the Quran among usul scholars?
A) The need to include all four attributes
B) The need for the definition to apply to both the whole Quran and each individual verse
C) The need to exclude hadith
D) The need to make the definition short

Key Takeaway
The definition of the Quran in Hanafi usul is not fixed; scholars selected attributes based on their definitional purpose, all agreeing on the four core attributes.

The Four Definitions of the Quran: Rationales and Scope
Explains why usuliyyun differ in defining the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four main definitions of the Quran given by usul scholars and explain the rationale behind each, including the author's two-attribute definition.

Core Idea
Scholars chose different attribute sets: all four, two (miraculous and revealed), three (excluding miraculous), or two (written and mutawatir).

The passage presents a spectrum of definitions for the Quran, each selecting a different combination of the four fundamental attributes. In this lesson, we examine each definition and the reasoning that supports it. Understanding these variations deepens our grasp of how definitions serve specific legal and pedagogical purposes.

Guided Path
1
Review the four attributes
Recall the four attributes: revealed, miraculous, written in musahif, mutawatir. These are the building blocks of all definitions.
2
Analyze the definition with all four attributes
Some scholars include all four for maximum clarity. They argue that definition aims at complete clarity (bayan).
This is the most comprehensive definition.
3
Analyze the definition with two attributes: miraculous and revealed
Another group uses only 'miraculous' and 'revealed' because in the Prophet's time, the Quran was not compiled in a mushaf and transmission was not needed.
This definition captures the essence without historical contingencies.
4
Analyze the definition with three attributes: revealed, written in musahif, mutawatir
A third group includes these three because they consider 'miraculous' not essential (only scholars recognize it) and not pervasive (only in complete speech).
This focuses on what is perceptible and certain.
5
Analyze the author's definition: written in musahif and mutawatir
The author of the matn (being commented on) uses only 'written in musahif' and 'mutawatir' to distinguish the Quran from other texts.
This is the most practical for differentiation.

اصولیین کی تعریفات میں وجہ اختلاف کا بیان
ہم کل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال:۔ اصولیین نے جو قرآن کی تعریفیں کیں ہیں وہ مختلف کیوں ہیں ؟ وجہ اختلاف کیا ہے؟
جواب:۔ میں شاریخ کہتے ہیں کہ اصولیین کے نزدیک جس طرح قرآن کا اطلاق مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے یعنی الحمد للہ سے والناس تک ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی ایک ایک آیت پر ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اصولی بحث کرتے ہیں اثبات الاحکام من الاولہ سے اور یہ استنباط آیت آیت سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مجموعہ سے فلہذا ان کو ایسی صفات کی ضرورت پڑی جو آیت آیت پر بھی صادق آئیں اور یہ مجموعہ پر بھی صادق آئیں اور وہ صفات چار ہیں۔

The Status of Basmalah in the Hanafi School: Early vs Later Positions
Internal Hanafi dispute on basmalah's Quranic status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on the basmalah and evaluate the evidence for the later position.

Core Idea
The basmalah's Quranic status in the Hanafi school: early scholars denied it except in Surah al-Naml; later scholars affirmed it for all surahs based on consensus of the Salaf.

This passage addresses a classical usul dispute within the Hanafi school: is the basmalah (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim) at the beginning of each surah part of the Quran? The early Hanafi scholars held a restrictive view, but later scholars revised the madhhab's position based on a powerful evidence from the practice of the Salaf. Understanding this evolution is crucial for applying the correct ruling in prayer and Quranic recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Locate the early position (mutqaddimin) that only the basmalah in Surah al-Naml is Quranic, and the later position (mutakhkhirin) that the basmalah at the start of every surah is a Quranic verse for separation.
The text uses 'المشهور من مذهب أبي حنيفة' for the early view and 'الصحيح من المذهب' for the later view.
2
Understand the evidence for each view
For the early view: only the verse in al-Naml is mutawatir. For the later view: the basmalah was written in the musahif in Quranic script without objection from the Salaf, indicating consensus.
The later view relies on a dalil of ijma (consensus) derived from the Companions' practice.
3
Recognize the tarjih (preference) in the madhhab
The passage states that the later view is considered 'al-sahih' (the correct) in the madhhab, despite the early position being more famous.
This reflects a development in Hanafi usul over time.
4
Apply the practical consequences
The thamarah al-khilaf: whether basmalah is recited aloud in prayer and whether it counts as a verse in Quranic tally. The later view affects rulings on jahr (loud recitation) in certain prayers.
This shows how a usul dispute directly impacts fiqh practice.

وَأَمَّا التَّسْمِيَّةُ فَالْمَشْهُورُ مِنْ مَذْهَبِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي كَثِيرٍ مِنْ كُتُبِ الْمُتَقَدِّمِينَ أَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ إِلَّا مَا تَوَاتَرَ بَعْضُ آيَةٍ مِنْ سُورَةِ النَّمْلِ ، وَإِنَّ قَوْلَهُمْ بِلَا شُبُهَةٍ احْتِرَازُ عَنْهَا إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُتَأَخْرِينَ ذَهَبُوا إِلَى أَنَّ الصَّحِيحَ مِنَ الْمَذْهَبِ أَنَّهَا فِي أَوَائِلِ السُّوَرِ آيَةٌ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ أُنْزِلَتْ لِلْفَصْلِ بَيْنَ السُّوَرِ بِدَلِيلِ أَنَّهَا كُتِبَتْ فِي الْمَصَاحِفِ بِخَطِّ الْقُرْآنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ إِنْكَارٍ مِنْ السَّلَفِ وَعَدَمُ جَوَازِ
And as for the basmalah, the famous [position] from the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, as mentioned in many books of the early scholars, is that it is not from the Quran except what was transmitted as a mutawatir part of a verse from Surah al-Naml. And indeed their saying 'without doubt' is a precaution against it. However, the later scholars went to the view that the correct [position] in the madhhab is that it is, in the beginnings of the surahs, a verse from the Quran revealed for separation between the surahs, with the evidence that it was written in the musahif in the script of the Quran without any objection from the Salaf, and the impermissibility of...
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage from the commentary addresses the status of the basmalah (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim) in the Hanafi school. It presents two positions: first, the well-known early Hanafi position (attributed to Abu Hanifa in many books of the early scholars) that the basmalah is not part of the Quran except for the part in Surah al-Naml (verse 30) which is mutawatir. The phrase 'without doubt' (bila shubhah) is a precaution to exclude any doubt about this. Second, the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) held that the correct view in the madhhab is that the basmalah at the beginning of each surah is a Quranic verse, revealed to separate between surahs. Their evidence is that it was written in the musahif in the script of the Quran with the consensus of the Companions (Sahabah) and the Salaf, without any objection. The passage cuts off mentioning another evidence: 'and the impermissibility of...' likely referring to it being recited in prayer. This is a classic usul dispute within the Hanafi school on the definition of what constitutes part of the Quran.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'.
متواتر (mutawatir): Transmitted by a large number ensuring certainty.
مصحف (mushaf): The written codex of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi scholars, what is the evidence that the basmalah at the beginning of surahs is part of the Quran?
A) It is mentioned in the Hadith.
B) It was written in the musahif in Quranic script without any objection from the Salaf.
C) The Prophet recited it aloud.
D) Abu Hanifa changed his view.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school developed its position on the basmalah: the later view (it is a Quranic verse for separation) is the correct one, based on the consensus of the Salaf.
