A) To emphasize that i'jaz is in words only
B) To align with Imam Abu Hanifah's terminology that the Quran is the combination of both words and meanings
C) To reject the possibility of Persian recitation in prayer
D) To avoid the impression that the Quran is only words

Key Takeaway
The inimitability (i'jaz) of the Quran is fundamentally a property of its Arabic words, arising from eloquence (balaghah), while the miraculousness of meanings is mediated through the arrangement (nazm) of those words.

Al-Quran as Source

Imam Abu Hanifa's Proof for Persian Recitation in Prayer
Presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proofs and subsequent conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's two proofs for allowing Persian recitation and list the five conditions that later scholars added.

Core Idea
Persian recitation is unconditionally valid; the purpose is meaning, not Arabic words.

This passage explains Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that reciting the Quran in Persian during prayer is permissible. The author presents two proofs: the linguistic scope (wus'at) of the Quran and the priority of meaning and spiritual connection. Interestingly, the concession is not conditional on hardship. Later, scholars added five conditions to preserve the integrity of the Quranic message.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling being justified
The ruling is that reciting the Quran in Persian in prayer is permissible. Note that this is a departure from the default requirement of Arabic.
2
Extract the first proof
The first proof is wus'at (scope) of the Quranic words, evidenced by the revelation of seven ahruf to ease recitation for different Arab tribes.
This indicates that the words themselves are not the sole focus; flexibility is built into the revelation.
3
Extract the second proof
The second proof is that the purpose of prayer is meaning and connection with Allah. Struggling with Arabic words can distract from this spiritual state, so Persian is allowed.
This is a rational argument based on the objectives of worship.
4
Classify the concession
The concession is a rukhsat isqat (dropping of an obligation) and is not conditional on hardship. This means Persian is allowed even if one can read Arabic.
This distinguishes it from a rukhsat tahfif which only applies when there is difficulty.
5
List the five conditions
Later scholars imposed conditions: 1) reciter is a Sunni, 2) words are unambiguous, 3) only short phrases, not enough to complete the prayer, 4) without intention to change the Quran, 5) only translation, not interpretation.
These conditions ensure that the practice does not lead to distortion of the Quranic message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ بل اعتبر المعنی :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلاحصہ ہے غرض یہ ہے کہ امام بوحنیف نے نماز میں فاری زبان میں قرات کو جائز قرار دیا تھا اس کی شاریح دلیل دیتے ہیں۔ دلیل: یہ ہے کہ الفاظ قرآن میں وسعت ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ جب قرآن قریش کی لغت میں اترا تو دوسرے قبائل نے شکایت کی کہ ہمارے لئے پڑھنا مشکل ہے تو سات قراء توں کی اجازت دی تو معلوم ہوا کہ وسعت ہے اگر وسعت نہ ہوتی تو سات قراءتوں کی اجازت نہ ملتی ۔ دوسری دلیل : مقصود معنی و مفہوم ہے الفاظ تو وہاں تک پہنچے کا وسیلہ ہیں خصوصاً جب نمازی نماز میں بارگاہ الہی میں ہوتا ہے تو مراقبہ اور اللہ کی رحمت کے مشاہدہ میں ہوتا ہے اس وقت معانی پڑھنے کی اجازت دی کیونکہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ الفاظ کی طرف توجہ کرنے سے تعلق الی اللہ اور حضوری کی کیفیت میں کمی آسکتی ہے کیونکہ الفاظ قرآن معجز ہیں الفاظ کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے کیفیت حضوری میں فرق آ سکتا ہے اس لئے فارسی میں قراءت کو جائز قرار دیا اور نماز کے حق میں لزوم تنظیم کی رخصت دے دی اور یہاں پر یہ رخصت کسی عذر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں بلکہ بلا عذر بھی نظم کو ترک کر کے غیر عربی میں قراءت جائز قرار دی کیونکہ یہ رخصت اسقاط ہے اور رخصت اسقاط عذر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوتی لیکن بعض حضرات نے اجازت کے لئے کچھ شرائط ذکر کی ہیں۔ (1) فارسی میں قراءت کرنے والا سنت کا پابند ہو بدعتی نہ ہو اگر بدعتی ہو تو اس کے لئے قرات بالفارسی جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۲) جوالفاظ فارسی میں ادا کرتا ہے وہ کئی معانی کا احتمال نہ رکھیں ورنہ غیر قرآن کا شائبہ ہوگا۔ (۳) ایک دو جملہ فارسی میں قرات کرے تب جائز ہے اور اگر اتنی مقدار پڑھے جس سے نماز پوری ہوتی ہے مثلا بڑی آیت کا ترجمہ یہ نا جائز ہے۔ (۴) بغیر قصد وارادہ کے الفاظ ادا کرے اگر ارادہ وقصد سے زبان سے ادا کرتا ہے تو دیکھا جائے گا مجنون ہے یا زندیق اگر مجنون ہے تو علاج کریں گے وگرنہ قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ (۵) وہ الفاظ صرف ترجمہ پر مشتمل ہوں تغییر پر مشتمل نہ ہوں اگر تفسیر پر مشتمل الفاظ ہوں تو غیر قرآن ہوگا اور نماز نہیں ہوگی۔
His saying: 'Rather, consider the meaning': This is the first part of the commentary's text. The purpose is that Imam Abu Hanifa had allowed recitation in the Persian language in prayer. The commentator gives proofs. Proof: that the words of the Quran have scope (wus'at). This is the reason that when Quran was revealed in the dialect of Quraysh, other tribes complained that it was difficult for them to read, so permission for seven ahruf was given. So it is known that there is scope. If there were no scope, permission for seven ahruf would not have been given. Second proof: The purpose is meaning and concept; words are a means to reach that, especially when the worshipper is in the court of Allah in prayer, he is in contemplation and observation of Allah's mercy. At that time, permission to read the meanings was given because it is possible that paying attention to words may decrease the connection to Allah and the state of presence. Because the words of the Quran are miraculous, focusing on words may affect the state of presence. Therefore, recitation in Persian was allowed, and concession was given regarding the obligation of order (nazm) in prayer. And here this concession is not specific to any excuse, rather even without excuse, leaving the order and reciting in non-Arabic is allowed because this concession is a concession of dropping (rukhsat isqat) and a concession of dropping is not specific to an excuse. But some people have mentioned certain conditions for permission: (1) The one reciting in Persian should be a follower of sunnah, not an innovator; if he is an innovator, Persian recitation is not permissible for him. (2) The words he utters in Persian should not carry multiple meanings, otherwise there would be suspicion of being non-Quran. (3) He should recite one or two sentences in Persian; if he recites an amount that completes the prayer, like the translation of a long verse, that is not permissible. (4) He should utter the words without intention and will; if he utters with intention and will, then it will be seen: is he insane or a heretic? If insane, he will be treated; otherwise, he will be killed. (5) Those words should consist only of translation, not of interpretation; if they consist of interpretive words, then it will be non-Quran and the prayer will not be valid.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's position on Persian recitation in prayer and its justification. The first proof is the scope (wus'at) of Quranic words, evidenced by the revelation of seven ahruf to ease recitation for different tribes. This indicates that the words themselves are not the sole focus. The second proof is rational: the purpose of prayer is meaning and connection with Allah; struggling with Arabic words may distract from this spiritual state. Thus, Persian is allowed even without excuse because the concession is a 'rukhsat isqat' (concession of dropping an obligation), which is not conditional on hardship. However, later scholars imposed conditions to ensure that the Persian words are faithful translations and not interpretations, and that the reciter is a Sunni. These conditions show a cautious approach to avoid altering the Quranic message.

Key Terms
وسعت (wus'at): Scope or flexibility in the words of the Quran, evidenced by the permission of seven ahruf.
رخصت اسقاط (rukhsat isqat): A concession that drops an obligation, not conditional on hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for Persian recitation?
A) The reciter must be unable to read Arabic
B) The words must not carry multiple meanings
C) The recitation must be the entire surah
D) The reciter must be a scholar

Key Takeaway
Persian recitation is unconditionally valid as per Abu Hanifa's proofs, but later scholars added five conditions to prevent deviation.

Istinbat of Reciting Quranic Meaning in Persian
Istinbat of permissibility of Persian qira'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling on reciting the Quran's meaning in Persian from Quran 73:20 using the principles of amm, khass, and takhsis.

Core Idea
The partitive 'min' in 'mā tayassara minh' allows the required portion to be the meaning alone — a composite part suffices.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary tackles a critical question: if the Quran is defined as Arabic words, how can reciting its meaning in Persian fulfill the prayer's obligation? The answer lies in the istinbat from the verse, the concept of khalifa, and a distinction between types of pillars. In this lesson, we will trace the Hanafi derivation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and its apparent generality
Locate the verse 'fa-iqra'ū mā tayassara minh' (Quran 73:20). The word 'mā' (ما) is a general term that encompasses any portion of the Quran.
General (amm) in Hanafi usul indicates all individuals of a category unless specified otherwise.
2
Recognize the partitive 'min' as a tool for takhsis
The 'min' (من) in the phrase is partitive (li al-tab'īḍ), meaning 'some of it'. This particularizes the general 'mā' to require only a part.
Hanafis take 'min' as partitive here due to the context of concession (rukhsa).
3
Distinguish between simple and composite parts
The required 'some' (ba'd) can be simple (a single ayah) or composite (the meaning alone, without the Arabic wording). The Hanafi position adopts the composite part interpretation.
The composite part is justified by the concept that meaning is the primary intention.
4
Apply the concept of khalifa to preserve the Quran's definition
The non-Arabic arrangement (e.g., Persian) serves as a khalifa (substitute) for the original Arabic nazm. By estimation (taqdīran), the attributes of Quran (transmission, writing) apply to this substitute, so the definition remains intact.
This concept is unique to Hanafis and prevents the definition from failing.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i counter-reading
Shafi'is maintain that 'mā' remains general, requiring recitation of any Arabic portion. They do not accept the composite part interpretation or the concept of khalifa.
The practical difference: Hanafis allow Persian recitation for non-Arabic speakers; Shafi'is require Arabic even if meaning is understood.

جواب (۲):۔ اس جواب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ہم دوسری شق اختیار کرتے ہیں کہ فقط معنی کو قرآن نہیں کہتے اس پر جو اشکال ہوا تھا کہ اس صورت میں یہ لازم آئے گا کہ نماز قرآت قرآن کے بغیر جائز ہو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ اشکال اس وقت لازم آئے گا کہ جب ہم یہ کہیں کہ نماز میں قرآن محدود ( یعنی وہ قرآن جس کی حد بیان کی گئی ہے) کی قراءت فرض ہے حالانکہ ہم ایسا نہیں کہتے بلکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ نماز میں معنی قرآن کی قراءت فرض ہے اور وہ پائی گئی ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے غیر عربی کے ساتھ اسی معنی کو تعبیر کیا ہے اور ہم نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ معنی قرآن کی قراءت فرض ہے وہ اس وجہ سے کہ امام صاحب نے فاقر اءوا ما تیسر منہ کو معنی پرمحمول کیا ایسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ان پر ظاہر ہوتی ہیں ہمیں معلوم نہ ہو۔ بعض نے کہا کہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ دلیل یہ ہو کہ ما تیسر منہ میں من تبعیض کے لئے ہو اس وجہ سے کہ یہاں تیسر سے رخصت بیان کی جارہی ہے اور رخصت تبعیض اور تخفیف سے ہی ہو گی لہذا جب من کو تبعیض کے لئے لیا تو یہاں دو چیزیں ہیں نظم اور معنی لہذا اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ بعض کی قرآت ضروری ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وہ بعض معنی ہے اور بعض نے کہا ممکن ہے دلیل یہ ہو کہ ما تیسر منہ میں یہ بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ بعض ما تیسر نماز لئے کافی ہے اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بعض ما تیسر کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) بعض بسیطی (۲) بعض ترکیبی بعض بسیطی یہ ہے کہ ایک آیت سے نماز جائز ہو اور بعض ترکیبی یہ ہے کہ نظم اور معنی میں سے صرف معنی پر اکتفا کرنا جائز ہو جب ما تیسر وا جب ہوا تو ان دونوں نوعوں میں سے ہر ایک بعض پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز ہوگا چاہے وہ ایک آیت کی تلاوت کرے اور چاہے تو فقط معنی کی قراءت کرے نماز ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل دی ہے دانہ بھی زیر الاولین حالانکہ پہلے صحیفے غیر عربی میں تھے تو معلوم ہوا کہ قرآن معانی کا نام ہے اس لئے فارسی میں قراءت جائز قرار دی۔
فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض اس سے سوال و جواب ہے۔ اعتراض:- یہ ہے کہ پہلے جواب دیا تھا کہ ما تیسر من القرآن میں ما عام ہے تو ایسی صورت میں حقیقت و مجاز کا اجتماع لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ ما کا حقیقی معنی الفاظ ہیں اور مجازی معنی معانی ہیں یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز ہے یہ احناف کے ہاں درست نہیں ہے
(3) If one recites a couple of sentences in Persian, it is permissible. But if one recites an amount that completes the prayer, like the translation of a long verse, it is impermissible.
(4) [The words] should be uttered without intention and purpose. If he utters with intention and purpose, then it will be seen: if he is insane, he will be treated; otherwise, he will be killed.
(5) Those words should consist only of translation, not of change (taghyir). If the words consist of interpretation (tafsir), then it will be non-Quran and the prayer will not be valid.
And as for the speech (wa amma al-kalam): This is the second part of the commentary's expression. From here, he points to the answer of a question. Question: You say that recitation of Quran is a pillar (rukn) of prayer, and you have defined Quran as words indicating meaning. Now, how can something be a pillar and not be necessary (lazim)? Now words are a pillar, and recitation in Persian is permissible. How was this pillar performed?
Answer: There are two types of pillar: (1) originally intended (maqsūd aṣlī), (2) not originally intended. A necessary pillar is that which is originally intended, and that which is not originally intended is not necessary. Here, since the originally intended is meaning, not words, therefore words are not necessary. More detail will come later. Is recitation only the name of meaning or not?
Fa-in qīl: This is the third part of the commentary's expression. The purpose is to raise a question and give two answers. Objection: We ask: Is meaning alone the Quran or not? If you say that meaning alone is Quran, then two problems necessarily arise: First, it would necessitate that arrangement (nazm) has no consideration in the Quran and its status remains nothing, while this is impossible because either nazm is the very Quran, as research indicates, or it is part of the Quran; in both cases, the separation of nazm from the Quran is impossible. The second problem is that the definition (hadd) given for the Quran would not apply to this Quran, because you have transmitted the definition as 'written in the mushafs, etc.' — how? While these restrictions are attributes of the words. And if meaning alone is not the Quran, then if someone recites in Persian, he has not recited the Quran, so it would be necessary to say that recitation of Quran in prayer is not obligatory (fard), because his prayer, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, is valid. Answer (1): He answers by adopting both alternatives. In the case of adopting the first alternative, we do not accept the two problems stated. Rather, we say that the reality of nazm in the Quran will not remain only when its khalīfa (substitute) is not present. But when its khalīfa is present, saying that nazm has no consideration is not correct. Imam Abu Hanifa has considered the khalīfa, and that khalīfa is the arrangement of non-Arabic with which recitation is performed. Similarly, the second problem (the definition not applying) also arises only when the khalīfa is not considered. But when Imam has considered the khalīfa, these attributes mentioned in the definition (transmission, writing, etc.) — although they are not literally proven for the nazm — they are proven for the estimation (taqdīr) because they are proven for its khalīfa; therefore, estimationally they are proven for it.
Answer (2): The summary of this answer is that we adopt the second alternative: we do not call meaning alone Quran. The objection raised was that in this case, prayer would be valid without recitation of Quran. The answer is that this objection would arise only if we say that recitation of the limited Quran (i.e., the one with the given definition) is obligatory in prayer, whereas we do not say that. Rather, we say that recitation of the meaning of Quran is obligatory in prayer, and that has been achieved because he expressed that same meaning with non-Arabic. And what we said that recitation of meaning of Quran is obligatory is because Imam Abu Hanifa interpreted 'fa-iqra'ū mā tayassara minh' (recite what is easy of it) as meaning, due to a proof that was apparent to him — we do not know it. Some said that perhaps the proof is that 'min' in 'mā tayassara minh' is partitive (li al-tab'īḍ), because 'tayassara' here expresses concession (rukhṣa), and concession is by way of partiality and reduction. Therefore, when 'min' is taken as partitive, there are two things here: nazm and meaning. Hence it is proven that recitation of a part is necessary, and we say that part is meaning. Others said that perhaps the proof is that 'mā tayassara minh' indicates that some of what becomes easy is sufficient for prayer. Now we say that 'some of what becomes easy' (ba'd mā tayassara) is of two types: (1) simple part (ba'd basīṭī) and (2) composite part (ba'd tarkībī). Simple part means that one ayah is sufficient for prayer; composite part means that it is permissible to suffice with only meaning, from among nazm and meaning. When 'mā tayassara' is established, then it is permissible to suffice with either of these two types: whether one recites one ayah or recites only the meaning, the prayer will be valid. The author of al-Hidayah gave the proof that previous scriptures were in non-Arabic, so it is known that 'Quran' is a name for meanings; therefore, he deemed recitation in Persian permissible.
Fa-in qīl: This is the last part of the commentary's expression. The purpose is question and answer. Objection: He had answered earlier that 'mā' in 'mā tayassara min al-Qur'an' is general (ʿāmm). In that case, combining literal (ḥaqīqah) and metaphorical (majāz) usage becomes necessary, because the literal meaning of 'mā' is words and the metaphorical meaning is meanings. This is combining between ḥaqīqah and majāz, which is not valid according to the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion from a Hanafi usul commentary on the ruling of reciting the Quran's meaning in Persian during prayer. The author begins by stating explicit rulings: reciting a couple of sentences in Persian is permissible, but reciting an amount that completes the prayer (e.g., translation of a long verse) is impermissible. Utterance must be without intention; if intentional, the person's mental state is considered. Words must be pure translation, not interpretative expansion.
Then the commentary addresses a central question: How can recitation be a pillar (rukn) of prayer if it is not obligatory (lāzim) when done in Persian? The answer distinguishes two types of rukn: those that are primarily intended (maqsūd aṣlī) and those that are not. In qira'at, the meaning is primary, not the words; hence the specific Arabic wording is not obligatory. Later, the discussion deepens: Is meaning alone considered Quran? If yes, then the definition of Quran (which includes being written in mushafs, etc.) would not apply, and the arrangement (nazm) would lose significance. If no, then recitation in Persian would not be Quran, leading to the conclusion that Quran recitation is not obligatory in prayer—contradicting Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that such prayer is valid. The author provides two answers. First, by accepting that meaning alone is Quran but using the concept of khalīfa (substitute): the non-Arabic arrangement serves as a substitute for the original Arabic arrangement, so the attributes of the definition (transmission, writing) apply by estimation (taqdīran). Second, by rejecting that meaning alone is Quran, and instead arguing that the obligation in prayer is to recite the meaning of Quran, not the specific Arabic words. This is proven from the verse 'fa-iqra'ū mā tayassara minh'—where 'min' indicates partiality, and the required 'some' (ba'd) can be the meaning (composite part) rather than a full ayah. The author of al-Hidayah further supports this by noting that earlier divine scriptures were in non-Arabic, showing that the essence is meaning. Finally, a usul objection is raised: interpreting 'mā' as general (ʿāmm) leads to combining its literal meaning (words) and metaphorical meaning (meanings), which is impermissible according to Hanafi usul (jam' bayn al-ḥaqīqah wa al-majāz). This objection is left unanswered here, indicating the debate continues.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A pillar of prayer; an essential component. Here distinguished between originally intended (maqsūd aṣlī) and not originally intended.
خلیفہ (khalīfa): A substitute for the original Arabic arrangement (nazm) when reciting in a non-Arabic language; the non-Arabic wording serves as a khalifa, carrying the same attributes by estimation.
حقیقت و مجاز (ḥaqīqah wa majāz): Literal and metaphorical usage of words. The objection states that applying 'mā' to both words and meanings combines both, which is invalid according to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi istinbat from Quran 73:20, how is the word 'min' (من) interpreted?
A) As a general word indicating all of the Quran.
B) As partitive (li al-tab'īḍ), indicating that only a portion is required.
C) As explanatory, clarifying the meaning of 'mā'.
D) As superfluous (ṣilah), having no effect on the meaning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives the permissibility of reciting the Quran's meaning in Persian from the partitive 'min' in Quran 73:20, combined with the concept of khalifa.

Al-Quran as Source

Hanafi Istinbat: Reciting Quran's Meaning in Non-Arabic
Analyzing the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara' to justify Persian translation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of amm and tab'id to the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' and derive the ruling that reciting the Quran's meaning in a non-Arabic language suffices in prayer.

Core Idea
The Quranic command 'recite what is easy' includes the meaning, not just the Arabic words, by virtue of the generality of 'ma' and the partiality of 'min'.

In this lesson, we examine how Imam Abu Hanifa derived the permissibility of reciting the Quran in Persian (or any non-Arabic language) using the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran'. The analysis reveals a sophisticated usul argument involving the categories of 'amm', 'tab'id', and the distinction between 'ibarat al-nass and dalalat al-nass. This was a major point of ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term
Locate the word 'ma' (ما) in the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran'. In Hanafi usul, 'ma' is a general (amm) particle that includes all possible referents unless specified otherwise.
The generality of 'ma' is the starting point; it potentially covers both words and meanings.
2
Analyze the particle 'min'
The particle 'min' in 'min al-Quran' indicates tab'id (partiality), meaning that only a part of the Quran is required to be recited. This is supported by the context of concession (taysir), which implies ease and reduction.
Tab'id is a key principle: the obligation is not to recite the entire Quran, but a part of it.
3
Determine the components of the Quran
The Quran has two aspects: the Arabic wording (nazm) and the meaning (ma'na). The general 'ma' and the partial 'min' together indicate that any part of these two components suffices.
Hanafis distinguish nazm and ma'na; Shafi'is bind the Quran to its Arabic wording.
4
Apply the principle of taysir
The verse is a concession (taysir), so it aims to make recitation easy. Reciting the meaning in a language the worshipper understands is easier than requiring Arabic. Therefore, the 'easy part' refers to the meaning.
This step uses the objective of the law (maqsad) to specify the general.
5
Derive the ruling
Reciting the meaning of the Quran in a non-Arabic language (e.g., Persian) fulfills the obligation of qira'ah in prayer. The prayer is valid because the meaning is the essence of the Quran.
The ruling applies to those who cannot recite Arabic; habitual use is discouraged.

Source Text

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج لیکن جب اس کا خلیفہ موجود ہوتو یہ کہناکہ نظم کا کچھ اعتبار ہیں رہا یہ میچ نہیں امام صاحب نے خلیفہ کا اعتبار کیا ہے وہ خلیفہ غیر عربی کا نظم ہے جس سے قرءات کی جائے گی اسی طرح دوسری خرابی ( تعریف کا عدم صدق) بھی اس وقت لازم آتی ہے جب خلیفہ کا اعتبار نہ ہو لیکن جب امام صاحب نے خلیفہ کا اعتبار کر لیا تو یہ صفات جو تعریف میں مذکور ہوئیں ( نقل کتابت وغیرہ) یہ اگر چہ نظم کے لئے حقیقتہ ثابت نہیں لیکن تقدیر اعظم کے لئے ثابت ہیں بائیں وجہ کہ یہ اس کے خلیفہ کے لئے ثابت ہیں لہذا القدیرا اس کیلئے ثابت ہیں۔
جواب (۲):۔ اس جواب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ہم دوسری شق اختیار کرتے ہیں کہ فقط معنی کو قرآن نہیں کہتے اس پر جو اشکال ہوا تھا کہ اس صورت میں یہ لازم آئے گا کہ نماز قرآت قرآن کے بغیر جائز ہو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ اشکال اس وقت لازم آئے گا کہ جب ہم یہ کہیں کہ نماز میں قرآن محدود ( یعنی وہ قرآن جس کی حد بیان کی گئی ہے) کی قراءت فرض ہے حالانکہ ہم ایسا نہیں کہتے بلکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ نماز میں معنی قرآن کی قراءت فرض ہے اور وہ پائی گئی ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے غیر عربی کے ساتھ اسی معنی کو تعبیر کیا ہے اور ہم نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ معنی قرآن کی قراءت فرض ہے وہ اس وجہ سے کہ امام صاحب نے فاقر اءوا ما تیسر منہ کو معنی پرمحمول کیا ایسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ان پر ظاہر ہوتی ہیں ہمیں معلوم نہ ہو۔ بعض نے کہا کہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ دلیل یہ ہو کہ ما تیسر منہ میں من تبعیض کے لئے ہو اس وجہ سے کہ یہاں تیسر سے رخصت بیان کی جارہی ہے اور رخصت تبعیض اور تخفیف سے ہی ہو گی لہذا جب من کو تبعیض کے لئے لیا تو یہاں دو چیزیں ہیں نظم اور معنی لہذا اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ بعض کی قرآت ضروری ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وہ بعض معنی ہے اور بعض نے کہا ممکن ہے دلیل یہ ہو کہ ما تیسر منہ میں یہ بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ بعض ما تیسر نماز لئے کافی ہے اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بعض ما تیسر کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) بعض بسیطی (۲) بعض ترکیبی بعض بسیطی یہ ہے کہ ایک آیت سے نماز جائز ہو اور بعض ترکیبی یہ ہے کہ نظم اور معنی میں سے صرف معنی پر اکتفا کرنا جائز ہو جب ما تیسر وا جب ہوا تو ان دونوں نوعوں میں سے ہر ایک بعض پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز ہوگا چاہے وہ ایک آیت کی تلاوت کرے اور چاہے تو فقط معنی کی قراءت کرے نماز ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل دی ہے دانہ بھی زیر الاولین حالانکہ پہلے صحیفے غیر عربی میں تھے تو معلوم ہوا کہ قرآن معانی کا نام ہے اس لئے فارسی میں قراءت جائز قرار دی۔
فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض اس سے سوال و جواب ہے۔ اعتراض:- یہ ہے کہ پہلے جواب دیا تھا کہ ما تیسر من القرآن میں ما عام ہے تو ایسی صورت میں حقیقت و مجاز کا اجتماع لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ ما کا حقیقی معنی الفاظ ہیں اور مجازی معنی معانی ہیں یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز ہے یہ احناف کے ہاں درست نہیں ہے
جواب:۔ یہ تب لازم آتا ہے جب دونوں اکٹھے مراد لیں الفاظ بھی اور معانی بھی ہم کہتے ہیں کہ فاقرؤا میں الفاظ کی تلاوت معلوم ہوئی عبارۃ اعص سے اور معانی کا جواز ثابت ہوا دلالت النص سے یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز نہیں ہے یا یوں کہیں گے کہ الفاظ کی قراءت کا جواز عبارۃ النص سے ثابت ہوا اور معانی کو اس پر قیاس کر لیں گے۔
( قَوْلُهُ بِغَيْرِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ الْفَارِسِيَّةَ وَغَيْرَهَا سَوَاءٌ فِي ذَلِكَ الحُكْمِ وَقِيلَ الْخِلافُ فِى الْفَارِسِيَّةِ لَا غَيْرُ .
) قَوْلُهُ حَتَّى لَوْ قَرَأَ آيَةٌ) إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ الْاعْتِيَادُ وَالْمُدَاوَمَةُ عَلَى الْقِرَاءَةِ بِالْفَارِسِيَّةِ لِلْجُنُبِ وَالْحَائِضِ بَلْ لِلْمُتَطَهِّرِ أَيْضًا ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ الْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ عَلَى أَنَّهُ تَجِبُ سَجْدَةُ التَّلَاوَةِ بِالْقِرَاءَةِ بِالْفَارِسِيَّةِ وَيَحْرُمُ لِغَيْرِ الْمُتَطَهِّرِ مَسُّ مُصْحَفِ كُتِبَ بِالْفَارِسِيَّةِ فَقَدْ جَعَلَ النَّظْمَ غَيْرَ لَازِمٍ فِي ذَلِكَ أَيْضًا فَلَا يَصِحُ قَوْلُهُ خَاصَّةً قُلْنَا بَنَى كَلامَهُ عَلَى رَأْيِ الْمُتَقَدِّمِينَ ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا نَصَّ عَنْهُمْ فِي ذَلِكَ ،
وَالْمُتَأَخِّرُونَ بَنَوُا الْأَمْرَ عَلَى الاحْتِيَاطِ لِقِيَامِ الرُّكْنِ الْمَقْصُودِ أعْنِى الْمَعْنَى . قَوْلُهُ لَكِنَّ الْأَصَحْ أَنَّهُ رَجَعَ إِلَى قَوْلِهِمَا عَلَى مَا رَوَى نُوحُ بْنُ أَبِي مَرْيَمَ عَنْهُ قَالَ فَخُرُ الْإِسْلام ؛ لِأَنَّ مَا قَالَهُ يُخَالِفُ كِتَابَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى ظَاهِرًا حَيْثُ وَصَفَ الْمُنَزَّلَ بِالْعَرَبِيِّ ، وَقَالَ صَدْرُ الْإِسْلامِ أَبُو الْيُسْرِ : هَذِهِ مَسْأَلَةٌ مُشْكِلَةٌ لَا يَتَّضِحُ لأحَدٍ مَا قَالَهُ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى ، وَقَدْ صَنَّفَ الْكَرْخِيُّ فِيهَا تَصْنِيفًا طَوِيلًا وَلَمْ يَأْتِ بِدَلِيلٍ شَافٍ . ترجمہ:۔ اس کا قول بغیر العربیت اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرکہ بیٹک فارسی اور اس کا غیر برابر ہیں اس حکم میں اور کہا گیا ہے که اختلاف فارسی میں ہے نہ کہ اس کے غیر میں۔
قولہ لوقر و آیتہ : اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ بیشک نہیں ہے جائز عادت بنانا اور ہمیشگی اختیارکرنا فارسی میں قراءت پر جنبی اور حائضہ کے لئے بلکہ مطہر کے لئے بھی پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ متاخرین اس مذہب پر ہیں کہ بیشک واجب ہے سجدہ
Al-Tarwīḥ li-Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ: But when his deputy (khalifa) is present, then saying that the arrangement (nazm) has no consideration is not correct. Imam (Abu Hanifa) gave consideration to the deputy, and that deputy is the arrangement in a non-Arabic language by which recitation is made. Similarly, the other defect (the definition not applying) also becomes necessary when the deputy is not considered. But when Imam gave consideration to the deputy, then these attributes mentioned in the definition (transmission, writing, etc.) — even though they are not truly established for the arrangement, they are established for the estimable greatness (taqdir a'zam) because they are established for its deputy, therefore they are established for it by estimation. Second answer: The summary of this answer is that we adopt the second possibility: that only the meaning is not called Quran. The objection raised — that in that case it would necessitate that prayer is valid without recitation of the Quran — the answer to this is that this objection would only apply if we say that the recitation of the limited Quran (i.e., the Quran whose limit has been described) is obligatory in prayer, whereas we do not say that. Rather we say that the recitation of the meaning of the Quran is obligatory in prayer, and that has been attained because he expressed the same meaning in non-Arabic. And we said that the recitation of the meaning of the Quran is obligatory because Imam carried 'faqra'u ma tayassara minhu' to meaning, due to a proof that was evident to him but unknown to us. Some said: perhaps that proof is that 'min' in 'ma tayassara minhu' is for partiality (tab'id), because concession is expressed through 'tayassara' and concession is only through partiality and lessening. So when 'min' is taken for partiality, there are two things here: arrangement (nazm) and meaning (ma'na). Therefore it is proven that recitation of a part is necessary, and we say that part is meaning. And some said: perhaps the proof is that in 'ma tayassara minhu' it is stated that some 'ma tayassara' is sufficient for prayer. Now we say that 'some of what is easy' is of two types: (1) partial simple, (2) partial composite. Partial simple is that one verse suffices for prayer. Partial composite is that it is permissible to be content with only the meaning from among arrangement and meaning. When it is established that 'ma tayassara' refers to both types, then it becomes permissible to suffice with any one of them, whether he recites one verse or he recites only the meaning, the prayer will be valid. The author of al-Hidayah gave the proof: 'Danah bihi (?)', even though the earlier scriptures were in non-Arabic, so it became known that Quran is the name of meanings, therefore recitation in Persian was deemed permissible. If it is said: This is the last part of the commentary's expression, the gist is a question and answer. Objection: It is that previously it was answered that 'ma' in 'ma tayassara min al-Quran' is general, so in such a case combining literal and metaphorical would be necessary because the literal meaning of 'ma' is words and the metaphorical meaning is meanings; this is combining literal and metaphorical, which is not correct according to Hanafis. Answer: This would be necessary only if both are intended together, words and meanings. We say that in 'faqra'u', the recitation of words is known from the explicit text ('ibarat al-nass), and the permissibility of meanings is proven from the indication of the text (dalalat al-nass); this is not combining literal and metaphorical. Or we could say: the permissibility of reciting words is proven from the explicit text, and meanings are analogized to it. (His statement: 'with other than Arabic' is an indication that Persian and other languages are equal in this ruling, and it was said: the dispute is only concerning Persian, not others. His statement: 'even if he recites one verse' is an indication that it is not permissible to make a habit and continuously recite in Persian for a junub or menstruating woman, nor even for one with wudu. So if it is objected: the later scholars hold that the prostration of recitation is obligatory upon reciting in Persian, and it is prohibited for one without wudu to touch a Quran written in Persian, so they have considered the arrangement not necessary in that matter also; then his statement 'specifically' is not correct. We say: he based his statement on the view of the earlier scholars, for there is no explicit text from them on that. The later scholars based the matter on caution because the intended pillar, i.e., meaning, is established. His statement: 'But the most correct is that he returned to their view [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] according to what Nuh ibn Abi Maryam narrated from him — he said: the pride of Islam, because what he said apparently contradicts the Book of Allah, since He described what was revealed as Arabic. And the pride of Islam Abu al-Yusr said: This is a difficult issue; what Abu Hanifa said is not clear to anyone. Al-Karkhi wrote a lengthy treatise on it but did not bring a sufficient proof. Translation: His statement 'with other than Arabic' indicates that Persian and other languages are equal in this ruling, and it was said that the dispute is only in Persian not in other than it. His statement 'qawluhu law qara'a ayah' indicates that it is not permissible to make a habit and persist in reciting in Persian for a junub and menstruating woman, nor even for one with wudu. So if it is objected that the later scholars are of the view that the prostration of recitation is obligatory upon reciting in Persian and it is prohibited for one without wudu to touch a mushaf written in Persian, then they have made the arrangement not necessary in that matter too, so his statement 'specifically' is not correct. We say: he based his statement on the view of the earlier scholars, for there is no explicit text from them on that. The later scholars based the matter on caution because the intended pillar, i.e., meaning, is established.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (So recite what is easy from the Quran, Qur'an 73:20) to justify the Hanafi position that reciting the meaning (ma'na) of the Quran in a non-Arabic language (like Persian) suffices in prayer. The discussion addresses two main objections: (1) that if only meaning is considered Quran, prayer would be valid without Quranic recitation; (2) that interpreting 'ma' (what) as including both words and meanings leads to combining literal and metaphorical usage (jam' bayn al-haqiqah wa al-majaz), which Hanafis reject. The author first explains that Abu Hanifa introduced the concept of a 'deputy' (khalifa) — the non-Arabic wording that stands in for the original Arabic arrangement (nazm). The attributes of Quran (transmission, writing, etc.) apply to this deputy by estimation (taqdir), not literally. To the first objection, the Hanafi response is that what is obligatory in prayer is the recitation of the meaning of the Quran, not the specific Arabic wording. This meaning is present in the non-Arabic translation. The proof is drawn from the verse itself: 'min' in 'ma tayassara minhu' indicates partiality (tab'id), meaning a part of the Quran is sufficient, and that part can be either the wording (simple part) or the meaning (composite part). The second objection is answered by distinguishing between two modes of textual proof: the explicit text ('ibarat al-nass) establishes the recitation of words, while the indication of the text (dalalat al-nass) establishes the permissibility of meanings. Thus, both are derived from the same text but through different mechanisms, avoiding a combination of literal and metaphorical intent. The author then shifts to Arabic commentary, noting that Persian and other non-Arabic languages are equal in this ruling. However, the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) differed from the earlier ones (mutaqaddimun) on related issues: they consider the prostration of recitation obligatory for Persian recitation and prohibit the impure from touching a Quran written in Persian. The author explains that the text's author relied on the earlier view, while the later scholars acted out of caution because the pillar (rukn) of meaning is established. Finally, a report from Nuh ibn Abi Maryam is cited that Abu Hanifa supposedly retracted his position and agreed with his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because his view apparently contradicts the Quranic description of the revelation as Arabic. However, the author notes that this issue remains difficult, and even al-Karkhi's treatise did not provide a fully satisfactory proof.

Key Terms
النَّظْمُ (al-nazm): The specific Arabic wording and arrangement of the Quranic text.
الْمَعْنَى (al-ma'na): The meaning or content of the Quran, which can be expressed in any language.
الخَلِيفَةُ (al-khalifa): The non-Arabic wording that acts as a deputy for the original Arabic nazm, carrying the same rulings by estimation (taqdir).
عِبَارَةُ النَّصِّ ('ibarat al-nass): The explicit, literal meaning of the text; here used for the ruling that words are recited.
دَلاَلَةُ النَّصِّ (dalalat al-nass): The implied or indicative meaning of the text; here used to permit recitation of meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation of 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran', which element of the verse is used to argue that a portion of the Quran suffices?
A) The word 'faqra'u' indicates command.
B) The particle 'min' indicates partiality (tab'id).
C) The word 'ma' is specific to words.
D) The phrase 'min al-Quran' means from the Quranic words.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits reciting the Quran's meaning in a non-Arabic language in prayer by relying on the generality of 'ma' and the partiality of 'min' in 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran'.

Al-Quran as Source

Types of Wad': Shakhsī and Naw'ī
Explaining the two types of wad' and justifying Fakhr al-Islam's wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between wad' shakhsī and wad' naw'ī, and explain why Fakhr al-Islam used 'form and root' instead of simply 'placement'.

Core Idea
Wad' includes both individual assignment and rule-based placement; the latter has two subtypes, one leading to metaphor.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary clarifies the two types of wad' (placement) and addresses a subtle question about terminology. By understanding these types, you will see how a single term like 'wad'' can be ambiguous, and why precision is crucial in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of wad'
Recognize that placement involves both the root (māddah) and the form (hay'ah). Both contribute to the word's indication of meaning.
2
Distinguish wad' shakhsī and naw'ī
Wad' shakhsī is individual assignment (e.g., proper nouns). Wad' naw'ī is rule-based placement, which has two subtypes: (a) setting a general rule for a class of words, and (b) a rule that yields metaphorical indication when a qarīna diverts from the original meaning.
The second subtype is a form of majāz.
3
Analyze the reason for Fakhr al-Islam's wording
If he had used the absolute term 'wad' li al-ma'nā', it might be misunderstood to exclude the second subtype of naw'ī (which is deficient compared to the first). By explicitly mentioning 'form and root', he removes that ambiguity.
The absolute term 'wad'' could be interpreted as only the first type or only shakhsī.
4
Appreciate the subtle benefit
Prioritizing 'form' over 'root' highlights that form carries the primary indication for commands and prohibitions, which are central in fiqh. The root material is shared across different forms.
This reflects a Hanafi emphasis on the role of hay'ah in conveying legal rulings.
5
Apply the classification to Quranic examples
For instance, a definite plural like 'السارقون' indicates generality by the first subtype of wad' naw'ī: every word with the form 'definite plural' indicates all individuals of its category.

lئے وضع کیا ہے اسی طرح اس نے اس کی ہیئت کو بھی معنی مفنی (گزرا ہوا) کیلئے وضع کیا ہے پس لفظ کی دلالت معنی پر دو چیزوں کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے (۱) وضع مادہ (۲) وضع ہیاۃ ۔ لہذا جب ان دونوں کو وضع میں دخل ہوا تو ان دونوں کو ذکر کر کے وضع مراد لے لیتے ہیں چنانچہ یہاں علامہ فخر الاسلام نے ایسے ہی کیا ہے کہ صیغہ والفتہ (بیا تا اور مادہ) بونکر وضع مراد لیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ جب صیغہ ولفتہ کے عنوان سے مقصود لفظ کی تقسیم وضع المعنی کے اعتبار سے ہے تو علامہ فخر الاسلام نے اس کو وضع للمعنی سے کیوں تعبیر نہیں کیا ؟ جبکہ اس میں اختصار بھی ہے؟ جواب (1):۔ جواب کو سمجھنے سے قبل ایک مقدمہ کا جانا ضروری ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ وضع کی دوقسمیں ہیں (۱) وضع شخصی اور وہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ کو معنی مخصوص کے مقابلہ میں متعین کرنا (۲) وضع نوعی پھر اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ اول: کوئی قاعدہ یا ضابطہ متعین کرنا کہ ہر وہ لفظ جو فلاں کیفیت کے ساتھ متصف ہوگا وہ فلاں معنی مخصوص پر دلالت کرے گا مثلا یوں کہنا کہ ہر وہ جمع کا صیغہ جو معرف باسلام ہو تو وہ اپنے مسمیات میں سے ہر سمجی پر دلالت کریگا۔ ثانی:۔ اس طرح کا ضابطہ بیان کرنا کہ ہر وہ لفظ جو معنی مخصوص کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہو قرینہ صارفہ ( یعنی اس معنی کے مراد نہ لینے پر) کے وقت اس کے متعلقات میں سے مخصوص متعلق پر دلالت کرے گا اب وضع نوعی کی یہ دوسری قسم مجاز کے قبیل سے ہے کیونکہ لفظ بیان معنی اصلی سے متجاوز ہو جاتا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب لفظ وضع کو مطلقا ذ کر کیا جاتا ہے تو یہاں وضع کی تیسری قسم مراد نہیں لی جاتی اس لئے کہ یہ پہلی دونوں قسموں سے ناقص ہے البتہ پہلی دونوں قسمیں مراد لی جاسکتی ہیں لیکن کسی کو وہم ہو سکتا ہے کہ شاید دوسری قسم بھی مراد نہ لے سکیں کیونکہ یہ اول قسم سے ناقص ہے تو اس وہم کے ازالہ کے لئے فخر الاسلام نے وضع کا لفظ ذکر نہیں کیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جواب (۲): علامہ فخر الاسلام نے جو عنوان ذکر کیا اس سے ایک قاعدہ معلوم ہوا کہ لفظ کی وضع لمعنی میں بہیات اور مادہ دونوں کو دخل ہے پھر بیاہ کو مقدم کر کے اس طرف اشارہ کیا کہ اکثر حقائق معنی پر بیاہ کے واسطہ سے دلالت کرتے ہیں خصوصا امرونہی کہ دین کے اکثر احکام کا مدار انہی پر ہیں اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ ان کا امر و نہی ہونا ہیاۃ اور شکل کے اعتبار سے ہے مادہ تو ان کے درمیان اور ان کے غیر میں برابر تحقق ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فخر الاسلام لفظ وضع پر اکتفاء کرتے اور یہ عنوان ذکر نہ کرتے تو یہ فوائد ولطائف معلوم نہ ہوتے ۔واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
He placed it for meaning. Similarly, he placed its form (hay'ah) for a past meaning. So the word's indication of meaning occurs with two things: (1) placement of the root (maddah), (2) placement of the form. Therefore, when both are involved in placement, they mention both and intend placement. Thus here, Fakhr al-Islam did the same: he mentioned 'form and root' and intended placement. Question: Since the title 'form and root' aims at the division of words according to placement for meaning, why did Fakhr al-Islam not express it as 'placement for meaning'? That would be more concise. Answer (1): Before understanding the answer, it is necessary to know a premise: placement has two types: (1) shakhsi placement—assigning a word to a specific meaning; (2) naw'i placement, which has two subtypes. First: setting a rule that every word with a certain quality will indicate a specific meaning—e.g., every plural form definite with 'al' indicates each individual among its referents. Second: stating a rule that every word placed for a specific meaning, when there is a qarinah sarifah (context diverting from that meaning), will indicate a specific related item. This second subtype is from the category of metaphor, because the word transcends its original meaning. The conclusion of the answer: when the word 'placement' is mentioned absolutely, the third type (which is deficient) is not intended; rather, the first two types can be intended. But one might suspect that the second type is not intended because it is deficient compared to the first. To remove this suspicion, Fakhr al-Islam did not mention the word 'placement'. And Allah knows best. Answer (2): From the title Fakhr al-Islam mentioned, a principle is learned: the placement of a word for meaning involves both form and root. He prioritized form to indicate that most indications of meanings occur via form, especially commands and prohibitions, on which most religious rulings are based. It is obvious that their being commands and prohibitions is due to form and shape, while the root is common between them and others. In summary, if Fakhr al-Islam had sufficed with the word 'placement' and not mentioned this title, these benefits and subtleties would not be known. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from a Hanafi usul work explaining why Fakhr al-Islam (likely al-Pazdawi) used the phrase 'form and root' (صیغہ والفتہ) instead of simply 'placement'. The commentator first establishes that a word's indication of meaning depends on two elements: the root (maddah) and the form (hay'ah). Both are aspects of wad' (placement). Therefore, Fakhr al-Islam explicitly mentioned both to refer to the complete concept of wad'. A question is raised: why not just say 'wad' li al-ma'na' for brevity? The first answer introduces a premise about types of wad': shakhsi (individual assignment, e.g., proper nouns) and naw'i (generic, rule-based). Naw'i has two subtypes: one establishing a general rule (e.g., a definite plural indicates all individuals), and another that leads to metaphor (majaz) when a qarinah diverts from the original meaning. The commentator explains that if the absolute term 'wad'' is used, it might be misunderstood to exclude the second subtype (which is deficient compared to the first). To avoid this, Fakhr al-Islam used a more explicit phrase. The second answer highlights a subtle benefit: by mentioning form first, Fakhr al-Islam indicates that most meanings (especially in commands and prohibitions) are conveyed through form, while the root material is shared across different forms. This reflects the Hanafi focus on usul al-fiqh, where commands and prohibitions are key.

Key Terms
وضع شخصي (wad‘ shakhsī): Assigning a word to a specific meaning in a one-to-one manner, like proper nouns.
وضع نوعي (wad‘ naw‘ī): Setting a general rule that a certain type of word indicates a certain type of meaning.
وضع مادة (wad‘ māddah): Placement of the root letters of a word, which contribute lexical meaning but not grammatical form.
وضع هيئة (wad‘ hay’ah): Placement of the form or pattern of a word, which indicates grammatical meaning (e.g., tense, person, number) and sometimes legal force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Fakhr al-Islam not simply use the term 'wad' li al-ma'na'?
A) Because it is incomplete without mentioning both form and root.
B) Because 'wad' for meaning' is ambiguous and could be misunderstood to exclude the second subtype of naw'ī placement.
C) Because he wanted to show that form is more important than root.
D) Because he was following a different school of thought.

Key Takeaway
Wad' is not monolithic; recognizing its types—shakhsī and naw'ī—is essential for correctly interpreting how words convey meaning in legal texts.

The Primary Indication of Mutlaq: Concept or Individual?
Objection and response on whether mutlaq indicates the concept or the individual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the primary indication of mutlaq and distinguish between conceptual and individual indication using the concept of qarina.

Core Idea
Mutlaq primarily indicates the concept; individual reference requires an external qarina.

A key principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh is understanding what a mutlaq (unrestricted) word originally indicates. Does it point to the abstract concept (mafhum) or to an individual instance (fard)? This lesson examines a classic objection and response based on the Quranic command 'tahriru raqabatin'. By analyzing this debate, you will grasp a foundational tool for interpreting legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector's claim
The objector argues that mutlaq indicates both concept and individual equally, citing the Quranic verse 'tahriru raqabatin' (freeing a neck). Since the command is fulfilled by freeing an actual slave, the word 'raqabah' must refer to an individual, not just the concept.
This is a surface-level literal reading.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position holds that mutlaq's primary indication is the concept. In the verse, the individual reference comes from an external qarina (contextual clue), namely the verb 'tahrir' (freeing), because you cannot free a concept.
The qarina is external to the word itself.
3
Examine the Quranic dalil
The word 'raqabah' is mutlaq. If it only indicated the concept, the command would be impossible. The Hanafi response explains that the feasibility of the command is due to the qarina, not the mutlaq's own indication.
The Quran is qat'i al-thubut, but its dalala is zanni here.
4
Understand the role of qarina
A qarina khariji (external clue) shifts the application from concept to individual. It does not change the original linguistic meaning of the mutlaq but directs how it is fulfilled in practice.
This principle prevents overextension of literal meanings.
5
Contrast with the opposing view
The opposing school (e.g., Shafi'i) may treat mutlaq as equally indicative of both. The Hanafi distinction leads to different hermeneutical approaches when encountering unrestricted terms in other texts.
The practical difference (thamarah) lies in how far one looks for qara'in.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ان ارید : سے شاریخ مصنف پر سوال کر رہے ہیں۔
سوال:۔ مصنف نے کہا تھا کہ اسم جنس اور صفت دو حال سے خالی نہیں اس کا مفہوم مراد ہوگا یا فرد دال اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مطلق کی دلالت صرف مفہوم پر ہوتی ہے۔ فرد پر دلالت نہیں ہوتی یہ غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلق کی دلالت جس طرح مفہوم پر ہوتی ہے اسی طرح فرد پر بھی ہوتی ہے اس کی دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے تحریر رقبتہ اس میں رقبتہ یہ مطلق ہے اب رقبہ کا مفہوم آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ فرد آزاد ہوگا۔
جواب: مطلق کی اصل دلالت مفہوم پر ہوتی ہے اور آیت کریمہ میں جو فرد پر دلالت ہو رہی ہے یہ خارجی قرینہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ قرینہ تحریر ہے کیونکہ آزاد مفہوم کو نہیں کیا جا سکتا کسی فرد کو ہی آزاد کریں گے۔
His statement 'in urida': The commentator raises a question against the author. Question: The author said that ism jins and sifat are not devoid of two states: either its concept (mafhum) is intended or an individual (fard) is indicated. From this it appears that the indication of mutlaq is only on the concept, not on the individual. This is wrong, because the indication of mutlaq is on the concept as well as on the individual. The proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'tahriru raqabatin' (freeing a neck). Here 'raqabah' is mutlaq. Now the concept of 'raqabah' (neck) is not freed; rather, an individual is freed. Answer: The original indication of mutlaq is on the concept. In the noble verse, the indication on the individual is due to an external qarina (indication), and that qarina is 'tahrir' because the concept cannot be freed; we only free an individual.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage contains a question and answer regarding the indication of mutlaq (absolute) words. The author previously implied that mutlaq only indicates the concept (mafhum) and not the individual (fard). The objector disagrees, arguing that mutlaq indicates both, citing the Quranic verse 'tahriru raqabatin' (freeing a neck). The word 'raqabah' is mutlaq. If mutlaq only indicated the concept, then the command would require freeing the abstract concept of 'neck', which is impossible. Rather, a specific individual slave (a human being) is freed. So mutlaq must indicate individuals. The commentator responds by refining the position: the primary and original indication of mutlaq is indeed the concept. The indication of an individual in the verse is due to an external qarina (contextual clue), namely the verb 'tahriru' (freeing). Freeing can only be applied to an actual person, not the abstract concept. Thus, the individual reference is secondary, derived from the qarina, not from the mutlaq itself. This is a classic Hanafi usul analysis: mutlaq primarily indicates the essence or concept, and the actual application to individuals requires contextual factors. This distinction is crucial for understanding how legal commands are interpreted.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): A word that indicates its concept without any restriction, e.g., 'raqabah' (neck/slave) in the verse.
مفہوم (mafhum): The conceptual meaning of a word, e.g., the idea of 'neck' or 'slave'.
فرد (fard): An individual instance of the concept, e.g., a specific slave person.
قرینہ خارجی (qarina khariji): An external contextual clue that specifies or restricts the meaning, e.g., 'tahrir' indicating that a real person must be freed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why does the mutlaq word 'raqabah' in the verse indicate an individual?
A) Because mutlaq always indicates individuals.
B) Because of the external qarina 'tahrir'.
C) Because the concept of 'raqabah' means individual.
D) Because the author made a mistake.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mutlaq primarily indicates the concept; contextual clues (qara'in) are necessary to apply it to individuals.

The Ba Proof: Mahr Obligatory at Contract
Deriving the obligation of mahr from the particle ba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi istinbāṭ from the particle bā’ in Q. 4:24 to derive that mahr is obligatory upon the marriage contract itself, and explain how the Shāfiʿī reading differs regarding the case of al-mufawwiḍah.

Core Idea
The Arabic particle 'ba' is a specific tool that binds the contract to wealth, making mahr inseparable and obligatory immediately.

This passage from 'Al-Talwīḥ' presents the Hanafi demonstration that the dower (mahr) is an integral obligation of the marriage contract. The key is the linguistic function of the particle 'ba' in the Qur’ānic verse 'an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum'. The Hanafī treat this particle as a 'ḥarf khāṣṣ' that implies ilṣāq (adhesion), yielding the ruling that upon a valid marriage, the mahr is due by the very fact of the contract. The lesson also unpacks the dispute with al-Shāfiʿī over the case of a woman married without a specified dower (al-mufawwiḍah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative Qur’ānic phrase
Locate the phrase 'an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum' in Sūrat al-Nisā 4:24. The 'bi' is the particle bā’.
2
Classify the particle bā’ in Hanafī uṣūl
In Hanafī uṣūl, the bā’ is a specific (khāṣṣ) particle that indicates ilṣāq (adhesion). This means it attaches the action (seeking) to the object (wealth) inseparably.
3
Link 'al-ibtighā’' to the marriage contract
The context of the verse (referring to marriage) shows that 'seeking' here means the valid marriage contract ('aqd ṣaḥīḥ).
4
Apply ilṣāq to derive obligation
Since the bā’ adheres the contract to wealth, wealth (mahr) becomes inseparable from the contract. Therefore, mahr must be obligatory by the contract itself.
5
Extend to the case of al-mufawwiḍah
Even if no mahr was specified at marriage, the obligation arose at contract; thus full mahr al-mithl is due upon consummation or death. This contrasts with al-Shāfiʿī’s view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله تعالى أن تبتغوا بأموالكم الباء لفظ خاص يوجب الإلصاق فلا ينفك الابتغاء أي الطلب وهو العقد الصحيح عن المال أصلا فيجب بنفس العقد) بخلاف الفاسد فإن المهر لا يجب بنفس العقد إذا كان فاسدا) خلافا للشافعي والخلاف ههنا في مسألة المفوضة أي التي نكحت بلا مهر أو نكحت على أن لا مهر لها لا يجب المهر عند الشافعي رحمه الله عند الموت وأكثرهم على وجوب المهر إذا دخل بها، وعندنا يجب كمال مهر المثل إذا دخل بها أو مات أحدهما.

وقوله تعالى قد علمنا ما فرضنا عليهم (خص فرض المهر أي تقديره بالشارع فيكون أدناه مقدرا خلافا له)؛ لأن قوله فرضنا معناه قدرنا وتقدير الشارع إما أن يمنع الزيادة أو يمنع النقصان والأول منتف؛ لأن الأعلى غير مقدر في المهر إجماعا فتعين الثاني فيكون الأدنى مقدرا، ولما لم يبين ذلك المفروض قدرناه بطريق الرأي والقياس بشيء هو معتبر شرعا في مثل هذا.

الباب أي : كونه عوضا لبعض أعضاء الإنسان وهو عشرة دراهم فإنه يتعلق بها وجوب قطع اليد، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى كل ما يصلح ثمنا يصلح مهرا

ترجمہ: اور اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ( ان تبغوا باموالکم یعنی طلب کرو تم اپنے مالوں کے ساتھ "با" لفظ خاص ہے واجب کرتا ہے۔ الصاق کو پس نہیں جدا ہوگی ابتغاء اس سے ) یعنی طلب ( اور وہ عقد صحیح ہے مال سے بالکل پس واجب ہے وہ مال نفس عقد کے ساتھ بخلاف عقد فاسد کے کہ مہر واجب نہیں ہو گا نفس عقد سے جب کہ ہو وہ ( عقد ) فاسد ( بخلاف امام شافعی کے اور اختلاف یہاں مفوضہ کے کے مسئلہ میں ہے یعنی وہ عورت جو نکاح کرے بغیر مہر کے یا نکاح کرے اس شرط پر کہ نہیں ہوگا مہر اس کے لیے تو نہیں واجب ہو گا مہر امام شافعی کے ہاں موت کے وقت تک ۔ اور ان کے اکثر وجوب مہر کے قائل
And His statement, the Exalted: 'that you seek (husbands) with your wealth' (an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum). The 'ba' is a specific word that necessitates adhesion; thus the seeking (i.e., the request, which is the valid marriage contract) cannot be separated from the wealth at all. So it is obligatory by virtue of the contract itself. Contrary to a void (fāsid) contract, for the dower is not obligatory by virtue of the contract itself if it is void. Contrary to al-Shāfiʿī. And the difference here is in the case of al-mufawwiḍah, i.e., the woman who marries without a dower or marries on condition that she has no dower: the dower is not obligatory according to al-Shāfiʿī, may Allah have mercy on him, at the time of death. Most of them are upon the obligation of dower when he has consummated with her. According to us, the full fair dower (mahr al-mithl) is obligatory if he consummates or if one of them dies.

And His statement, the Exalted: 'We have known what We have prescribed for them' (qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim). He specified the prescription of the dower, i.e., its determination by the Lawgiver, so its minimum is fixed, contrary to him (al-Shāfiʿī). Because His word 'faraḍnā' means 'we have determined'. And the determination of the Lawgiver either prevents increase or prevents decrease. The first is negated because the maximum is not determined in dower by consensus. So the second is fixed, so the minimum is determined. And since He did not specify that which is prescribed, we determined it by way of opinion and analogy with something that is legally considered in such matters: the chapter, i.e., being a compensation for some parts of a human being, and it is ten dirhams, for the obligation of cutting the hand is connected to it. And according to al-Shāfiʿī, may Allah have mercy on him, everything that is suitable as a price is suitable as a dower.

Translation: And the statement of Allah, the Exalted (an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum, i.e., seek you with your wealth): 'ba' is a specific word, making adhesion obligatory. So the seeking (i.e., the request) will not be separated from it (i.e., wealth), that is the request, and it is the valid contract. So it is obligatory, that wealth, by virtue of the contract itself, contrary to a void contract, that the dower is not obligatory by virtue of the contract itself when it (the contract) is void. Contrary to Imam al-Shāfiʿī, and the disagreement here is regarding the issue of the mufawwiḍah, i.e., the woman who marries without a dower or marries on condition that there is no dower for her. The dower is not obligatory according to Imam al-Shāfiʿī up to the time of death, and most of them (his followers) hold the obligation of dower when he has consummated with her.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi istinbāṭ (derivation) of the obligation of mahr from the Qur'anic verse 'an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum' (Surah al-Nisā 4:24). The Hanafi argument: the particle 'ba' (ب) is a 'ḥarf khāṣṣ' meaning it indicates adhesion (ilṣāq). The 'ibtighā'' (seeking) refers to the valid marriage contract. Since the 'ba' adheres the seeking to wealth, it means that the mahr is inseparable from the contract. Therefore, upon a valid contract, the mahr becomes obligatory immediately (yajibu bi-nafs al-ʿaqd). This applies even if the mahr was not specified at the time of marriage (case of mufawwiḍah). According to Hanafis, if the husband consummates or one of them dies, the full mahr al-mithl is due. Shāfiʿī differs: he holds that in a marriage without specified mahr, no mahr is due until death or consummation? Actually the text says 'at the time of death' according to some Shāfiʿīs? The passage says 'لا يجب المهر عند الشافعي عند الموت' — it seems some Shāfiʿīs say mahr is not due until death? It says 'وأكثرهم على وجوب المهر إذا دخل بها' — most of them hold it is due upon consummation. Hanafi position is that mahr is due upon contract itself, but the amount becomes due upon consummation or death. The second verse 'qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim' (Surah al-Aḥzāb 33:50) is used to argue that the minimum mahr is fixed by the Lawgiver. Since Allah says 'faraḍnā' (We have prescribed), it indicates a determination. The minimum is deduced by analogy (qiyās) with the minimum amount for cutting of the hand (sariqa) which is ten dirhams. Thus, the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. Shāfiʿī holds that any amount can be mahr, not fixed minimum. This shows how Hanafi usul uses linguistic analysis and qiyās to derive fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
باء (bāʾ): The particle 'ba' which, according to the author, is a specific (khāṣṣ) word that necessitates adhesion (ilṣāq) between the verb and the object of the preposition.
مهر (mahr): The bridal gift obligatory upon the husband by virtue of the marriage contract.
مفوضة (mufawwiḍah): A woman who marries without specifying a dower (mahr) or on condition of no dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafī proof that mahr becomes obligatory immediately upon a valid marriage contract?
A) The consensus of the Companions that mahr must be specified.
B) The particle 'ba' in 'an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum' indicates adhesion, making mahr inseparable from the contract.
C) The verse 'qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim' fixes the minimum mahr.
D) The hadith 'No marriage without a wali and mahr'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that mahr is obligatory upon contract derives from the particle ba, which as a specific word for adhesion makes the dower an inseparable part of the marriage.

Deriving the Minimum Mahr: Qiyas with Hadd al-Sariqa
Deriving the minimum mahr via qiyās from the hadd al-sariqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi derivation of the minimum mahr (ten dirhams) from the verse 'qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim' via qiyās with the threshold for cutting the thief's hand, and compare it with the Shāfiʿī view of no fixed minimum.

Core Idea
The Lawgiver’s word 'faraḍnā' implies a fixed minimum; since no maximum is set, the minimum is derived by analogy with the hadd for theft: ten dirhams.

The second part of the passage addresses the determination of the minimum dower. Using the Qur’ānic verse 'qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim' (Sūrat al-Aḥzāb 33:50), the Hanafī argue that the Lawgiver has fixed a minimum mahr. They then derive that minimum by analogy (qiyās) with the minimum amount that triggers the cutting of the hand for theft (ḥadd al-sariqa), which is ten dirhams. This lesson examines that qiyās and contrasts it with al-Shāfiʿī’s view that any valuable item can serve as mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second proof text
The verse 'qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim' (Sūrat al-Aḥzāb 33:50) is cited. The word 'faraḍnā' (We have prescribed) indicates that the Lawgiver has set a fixed determination (qadr).
2
Analyze the meaning of 'faraḍnā'
In Hanafī usūl, 'farḍ' means determination (taqdīr). The verse states that Allah has already determined the mahr. This determination must be either a maximum or a minimum.
3
Eliminate the possibility of a fixed maximum
There is no maximum limit for mahr by consensus (ijmā‘). So the determination must refer to a minimum. Therefore, the minimum mahr is fixed by the Lawgiver.
4
Find the minimum via qiyās
Since the exact minimum is not explicitly stated in the verse or hadith, the Hanafīs resort to analogy. They find a similar figure in the Sharī‘a: the minimum amount for cutting the hand of a thief, which is ten dirhams.
5
Justify the analogy
Both mahr and the hadd al-sariqa involve monetary value. The rationale (ʿilla) is that ten dirhams is a value that is legally significant as a threshold. Therefore, the minimum mahr is set at ten dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله تعالى أن تبتغوا بأموالكم الباء لفظ خاص يوجب الإلصاق فلا ينفك الابتغاء أي الطلب وهو العقد الصحيح عن المال أصلا فيجب بنفس العقد) بخلاف الفاسد فإن المهر لا يجب بنفس العقد إذا كان فاسدا) خلافا للشافعي والخلاف ههنا في مسألة المفوضة أي التي نكحت بلا مهر أو نكحت على أن لا مهر لها لا يجب المهر عند الشافعي رحمه الله عند الموت وأكثرهم على وجوب المهر إذا دخل بها، وعندنا يجب كمال مهر المثل إذا دخل بها أو مات أحدهما.

وقوله تعالى قد علمنا ما فرضنا عليهم (خص فرض المهر أي تقديره بالشارع فيكون أدناه مقدرا خلافا له)؛ لأن قوله فرضنا معناه قدرنا وتقدير الشارع إما أن يمنع الزيادة أو يمنع النقصان والأول منتف؛ لأن الأعلى غير مقدر في المهر إجماعا فتعين الثاني فيكون الأدنى مقدرا، ولما لم يبين ذلك المفروض قدرناه بطريق الرأي والقياس بشيء هو معتبر شرعا في مثل هذا.

الباب أي : كونه عوضا لبعض أعضاء الإنسان وهو عشرة دراهم فإنه يتعلق بها وجوب قطع اليد، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى كل ما يصلح ثمنا يصلح مهرا

ترجمہ: اور اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ( ان تبغوا باموالکم یعنی طلب کرو تم اپنے مالوں کے ساتھ "با" لفظ خاص ہے واجب کرتا ہے۔ الصاق کو پس نہیں جدا ہوگی ابتغاء اس سے ) یعنی طلب ( اور وہ عقد صحیح ہے مال سے بالکل پس واجب ہے وہ مال نفس عقد کے ساتھ بخلاف عقد فاسد کے کہ مہر واجب نہیں ہو گا نفس عقد سے جب کہ ہو وہ ( عقد ) فاسد ( بخلاف امام شافعی کے اور اختلاف یہاں مفوضہ کے کے مسئلہ میں ہے یعنی وہ عورت جو نکاح کرے بغیر مہر کے یا نکاح کرے اس شرط پر کہ نہیں ہوگا مہر اس کے لیے تو نہیں واجب ہو گا مہر امام شافعی کے ہاں موت کے وقت تک ۔ اور ان کے اکثر وجوب مہر کے قائل
And His statement, the Exalted: 'that you seek (husbands) with your wealth' (an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum). The 'ba' is a specific word that necessitates adhesion; thus the seeking (i.e., the request, which is the valid marriage contract) cannot be separated from the wealth at all. So it is obligatory by virtue of the contract itself. Contrary to a void (fāsid) contract, for the dower is not obligatory by virtue of the contract itself if it is void. Contrary to al-Shāfiʿī. And the difference here is in the case of al-mufawwiḍah, i.e., the woman who marries without a dower or marries on condition that she has no dower: the dower is not obligatory according to al-Shāfiʿī, may Allah have mercy on him, at the time of death. Most of them are upon the obligation of dower when he has consummated with her. According to us, the full fair dower (mahr al-mithl) is obligatory if he consummates or if one of them dies.

And His statement, the Exalted: 'We have known what We have prescribed for them' (qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim). He specified the prescription of the dower, i.e., its determination by the Lawgiver, so its minimum is fixed, contrary to him (al-Shāfiʿī). Because His word 'faraḍnā' means 'we have determined'. And the determination of the Lawgiver either prevents increase or prevents decrease. The first is negated because the maximum is not determined in dower by consensus. So the second is fixed, so the minimum is determined. And since He did not specify that which is prescribed, we determined it by way of opinion and analogy with something that is legally considered in such matters: the chapter, i.e., being a compensation for some parts of a human being, and it is ten dirhams, for the obligation of cutting the hand is connected to it. And according to al-Shāfiʿī, may Allah have mercy on him, everything that is suitable as a price is suitable as a dower.

Translation: And the statement of Allah, the Exalted (an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum, i.e., seek you with your wealth): 'ba' is a specific word, making adhesion obligatory. So the seeking (i.e., the request) will not be separated from it (i.e., wealth), that is the request, and it is the valid contract. So it is obligatory, that wealth, by virtue of the contract itself, contrary to a void contract, that the dower is not obligatory by virtue of the contract itself when it (the contract) is void. Contrary to Imam al-Shāfiʿī, and the disagreement here is regarding the issue of the mufawwiḍah, i.e., the woman who marries without a dower or marries on condition that there is no dower for her. The dower is not obligatory according to Imam al-Shāfiʿī up to the time of death, and most of them (his followers) hold the obligation of dower when he has consummated with her.

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi istinbāṭ (derivation) of the obligation of mahr from the Qur'anic verse 'an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum' (Surah al-Nisā 4:24). The Hanafi argument: the particle 'ba' (ب) is a 'ḥarf khāṣṣ' meaning it indicates adhesion (ilṣāq). The 'ibtighā'' (seeking) refers to the valid marriage contract. Since the 'ba' adheres the seeking to wealth, it means that the mahr is inseparable from the contract. Therefore, upon a valid contract, the mahr becomes obligatory immediately (yajibu bi-nafs al-ʿaqd). This applies even if the mahr was not specified at the time of marriage (case of mufawwiḍah). According to Hanafis, if the husband consummates or one of them dies, the full mahr al-mithl is due. Shāfiʿī differs: he holds that in a marriage without specified mahr, no mahr is due until death or consummation? Actually the text says 'at the time of death' according to some Shāfiʿīs? The passage says 'لا يجب المهر عند الشافعي عند الموت' — it seems some Shāfiʿīs say mahr is not due until death? It says 'وأكثرهم على وجوب المهر إذا دخل بها' — most of them hold it is due upon consummation. Hanafi position is that mahr is due upon contract itself, but the amount becomes due upon consummation or death. The second verse 'qad ʿalimnā mā faraḍnā ʿalayhim' (Surah al-Aḥzāb 33:50) is used to argue that the minimum mahr is fixed by the Lawgiver. Since Allah says 'faraḍnā' (We have prescribed), it indicates a determination. The minimum is deduced by analogy (qiyās) with the minimum amount for cutting of the hand (sariqa) which is ten dirhams. Thus, the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. Shāfiʿī holds that any amount can be mahr, not fixed minimum. This shows how Hanafi usul uses linguistic analysis and qiyās to derive fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
قدر (qadr): Determination or fixation of the dower amount by the Lawgiver.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The fair dower determined by the dowers of similar women (e.g., paternal female relatives).
حد السرقة (ḥadd al-sariqa): The fixed punishment for theft, which includes cutting the hand when the stolen amount reaches the niṣāb.

C) From the verse 'an tabtaghū bi-amwālikum'.
D) By consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī fix the minimum mahr at ten dirhams via qiyās with the ḥadd al-sariqa, based on the Qur'ānic indication that the Lawgiver has determined a minimum.

Deriving Mahr Obligation from Quran 4:24 and the Dispute with al-Shafi'i
Textual analysis of Quran 4:24 to derive mahr obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a specific word (lafz khass) indicates immediate attachment to derive the obligation of mahr from Quran 4:24, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The letter 'ba' in Quran 4:24 makes mahr wajib upon the contract itself, not at death or consummation.

This passage demonstrates how the Hanafi school extracts a ruling from a single linguistic element. The letter 'ba' is treated as a specific textual indicator (lafz khass) that necessitates attachment (ilṣāq) between the marriage contract and the wealth. This leads to the ruling that mahr is obligatory immediately upon the valid contract. The passage then contrasts this with the Shafi'i view, which delays obligation in a tafwid marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative term
Find the word 'ba' in Quran 4:24 'an tabtaghu bi-amwalikum'. Classify it as a lafz khass.
Khass is specific and not open to general interpretation.
2
Derive the linguistic implication
The 'ba' indicates ilṣāq (attachment). So the seeking (marriage) is attached to wealth, making mahr inseparable from the contract.
3
State the ruling
Mahr becomes wajib at the moment of the valid contract.
This applies to valid, not invalid, marriages.
4
Compare with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that mahr is not wajib until death or consummation in a tafwid marriage, because no amount was specified.
Their evidence: the contract is silent on mahr.
5
Identify the consequence
If divorce occurs before consummation in a tafwid marriage, Hanafi: half mahr al-mithl is due. Shafi'i: no mahr due.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقَوْله تَعَالَى ) أَنْ تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمُ الْبَاء ُ لَفُظْ خَاصٌ يُوجِبُ الْإِلْصَاقَ فَلَا يَنْفَكُ الِابْتِغَاء أَى : الطَّلَبُ وَهُوَ الْعَقْدُ الصَّحِيحُ عَنْ الْمَالِ أَصْلًا فَيَجِبُ بِنَفْسِ الْعَقْدِ ) بِخِلَافِ الْفَاسِدِ فَإِنَّ الْمَهْرَ لَا يَجِبُ بِنَفْسِ الْعَقْدِ إِذَا كَانَ فَاسِدًا ) خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي وَالْخِلَافَ هَاهُنَا فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْمُفَوِّضَةِ أَى : الَّتِي نَكَحَتُ بِلا مَهْرٍ أَوْ نَكَحَتْ عَلَى أَنْ لَا مَهْرَ لَهَا لَا يَجِبُ الْمَهْرُ عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ عِندَ الْمَوْتِ وَأَكْثَرُهُمْ عَلَى وُجُوبِ الْمَهْرِ إِذَا دَخَلَ بِهَا ، وَعِنْدَنَا يَجِبُ كَمَالُ مَهْرٍ الْمِثْلِ إِذَا دَخَلَ بِهَا أَوْ مَاتَ أَحَدُهُمَا ) وقَوْله تَعَالَى ) قَدْ عَلِمْنَا مَا فَرَضْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ ( خَصَّ فَرُضَ الْمَهْر أَي تَقْدِيرَهُ بِالشَّارِعِ فَيَكُونُ أَدْنَاهُ مُقَدَّرًا خِلَافًا لَهُ ) ؛ لأنَّ قَوْلَهُ فَرَضْنَا مَعْنَاهُ قَدَّرُنَا وَتَقْدِيرُ الشَّارِعِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَمْنَعَ الزِّيَادَةَ أَوْ يَمْنَعَ النُّقْصَانَ وَالْأَوَّلُ مُنتفٍ ؛ لِأَنَّ الْأَعْلَى غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرٍ فِي الْمَهْرِ إجْمَاعًا فَتَعَيَّنَ الثَّانِي فَيَكُونُ الْأدْنَى مُقَدَّرًا ، وَلَمَّا لَمْ يُبَيِّنُ ذَلِكَ الْمَفْرُوضَ قَدْرُنَاهُ بِطَرِيقِ الرَّأْيِ وَالْقِيَاسِ بِشَيْءٍ هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ شَرُعًا فِي مِثْلٍ هَذَا الْبَابِ أَى : كَوْنُهُ عِوَضًا لِبَعْضِ أَعْضَاءِ الْإِنْسَانِ وَهُوَ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا وُجُوبُ قَطْعِ الْيَدِ ، وَعِندَ الشَّافِعِيِّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كُلُّ مَا يَصْلُحُ ثَمَنًا يَصْلُحُ مَهْرًا
And His saying, exalted be He, 'that you seek with your wealth' — the letter 'ba' is a specific word that necessitates attachment, so the seeking (i.e., the valid contract) is not separated from the wealth; thus it is obligatory with the contract itself. Contrary to the invalid (contract), for the dower is not obligatory with the contract itself when it is invalid. Contrary to al-Shafi'i, and the disagreement here is regarding the case of al-mufawwida, i.e., she who marries without dower or marries on the condition that there is no dower for her: the dower is not obligatory according to al-Shafi'i may Allah have mercy on him until death, and most of them (his followers) hold the dower obligatory when he has consummated with her. And according to us, a full dower of the like is obligatory when he has consummated with her or one of them dies. And His saying, exalted be He, 'We have known what We have prescribed for them' (33:38) — He specified the prescription of the dower i.e., its determination by the Lawgiver, so its minimum is determined, contrary to him (al-Shafi'i). Because His word 'faradna' means 'we have determined' and the determination of the Lawgiver either prevents increase or prevents decrease; the first is negated because the maximum is not determined in the dower by consensus, so the second is confirmed, thus the minimum is determined. And since that prescribed (amount) was not explained, we determined it by way of opinion and analogy with something that is legally considered in such a chapter, i.e., its being a compensation for some parts of a human: it is ten dirhams, for the obligation of cutting off the hand is attached to them. And according to al-Shafi'i may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him, everything valid as a price is valid as a dower.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of mahr (dower) in marriage, deriving the obligation and minimum value from Quranic texts and qiyas (analogy). The author first addresses verse 4:24 'an tabtaghu bi-amwalikum', focusing on the letter 'ba' which indicates attachment (ilṣāq). The argument is that since the 'ba' attaches the seeking (i.e., the marriage contract) to wealth (mahr), the mahr becomes obligatory immediately upon the contract itself in a valid marriage. This is contradicted by Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that in a tafwid marriage (where no mahr is specified), mahr is not obligatory until death or consummation. The Hanafi position is that mahr is wajib from the contract, though payment may be deferred. The passage then moves to verse 33:38 'qad 'alimna ma faradna 'alayhim', interpreting 'faradna' as 'we have determined' (taqdir). Since the Lawgiver determined the mahr, it implies a minimum limit; otherwise determination would be meaningless. The maximum is left open by consensus, so the minimum must be fixed. As the Quran does not specify the amount, the author uses qiyas: comparing mahr to the minimum value for stealing (nisaab) which triggers hand-cutting (10 dirhams), since both involve compensation. Thus the minimum mahr is set at ten dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, allowing any valid price as mahr. The commentary follows the author's order: proof from verse 4:24, then the dispute, then the proof from verse 33:38 and qiyas.

Key Terms
الباء (al-bā'): The letter 'ba' in the verse, indicates attachment (ilṣāq).
المفوضة (al-mufawwiḍa): Woman who marries without specifying dower.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Dower of the like, applicable when no dower is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only after consummation.
B) At the moment of the contract.
C) Only after death.
D) It becomes wajib only if specified.

Key Takeaway
The 'ba' in Quran 4:24 is a lafz khass obligating mahr from the moment of the valid contract in Hanafi usul.
