Deriving the Minimum Mahr: The Role of Qiyas on Theft Hadd
Qiyas derived minimum mahr from theft hadd and text inference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul method of qiyas to determine the minimum mahr by analogy with the minimum nisab for theft, and explain how the word 'faradna' in Quran 33:38 implies a fixed minimum.

Core Idea
Since Allah determined the mahr, its minimum must be fixed; analogy with theft gives 10 dirhams.

This part of the passage shows how the Hanafi school uses both textual implication and qiyas to fill a gap left by the Quran. The verse 'We have known what We have prescribed for them' indicates that the Lawgiver set a limit. Since the maximum is open by consensus, the minimum must be fixed. Then, through qiyas with the minimum value that triggers hand-cutting, the school arrives at ten dirhams as the minimum mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic indication
Quran 33:38 'qad 'alimna ma faradna 'alayhim': the word 'faradna' means 'We have determined'. This shows the Lawgiver set a limit.
'Faradna' implies taqdir (determination of quantity).
2
Analyze the nature of determination
Determination must either set a maximum or a minimum. The maximum is not fixed by consensus (ijma), so the determination must set a minimum.
This is an inference from the verse.
3
Establish the need for qiyas
Since the exact amount is not given in the text, we use qiyas to find it.
Qiyas is valid when there is an effective cause ('illa).
4
Identify the original case (asl)
The nisab for cutting the thief's hand is 10 dirhams. This is legally recognized as compensation for a body part.
The hadd of theft is established by Quran and Sunnah.
5
Draw the analogy
Mahr is also a compensation (for marital rights). The common 'illa is that both are compensations for parts of a human. Thus the minimum for mahr is analogized to the minimum for theft, i.e., 10 dirhams.
This is qiyas jali (clear analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقَوْله تَعَالَى ) أَنْ تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمُ الْبَاء ُ لَفُظْ خَاصٌ يُوجِبُ الْإِلْصَاقَ فَلَا يَنْفَكُ الِابْتِغَاء أَى : الطَّلَبُ وَهُوَ الْعَقْدُ الصَّحِيحُ عَنْ الْمَالِ أَصْلًا فَيَجِبُ بِنَفْسِ الْعَقْدِ ) بِخِلَافِ الْفَاسِدِ فَإِنَّ الْمَهْرَ لَا يَجِبُ بِنَفْسِ الْعَقْدِ إِذَا كَانَ فَاسِدًا ) خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي وَالْخِلَافَ هَاهُنَا فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْمُفَوِّضَةِ أَى : الَّتِي نَكَحَتُ بِلا مَهْرٍ أَوْ نَكَحَتْ عَلَى أَنْ لَا مَهْرَ لَهَا لَا يَجِبُ الْمَهْرُ عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ عِندَ الْمَوْتِ وَأَكْثَرُهُمْ عَلَى وُجُوبِ الْمَهْرِ إِذَا دَخَلَ بِهَا ، وَعِنْدَنَا يَجِبُ كَمَالُ مَهْرٍ الْمِثْلِ إِذَا دَخَلَ بِهَا أَوْ مَاتَ أَحَدُهُمَا ) وقَوْله تَعَالَى ) قَدْ عَلِمْنَا مَا فَرَضْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ ( خَصَّ فَرُضَ الْمَهْر أَي تَقْدِيرَهُ بِالشَّارِعِ فَيَكُونُ أَدْنَاهُ مُقَدَّرًا خِلَافًا لَهُ ) ؛ لأنَّ قَوْلَهُ فَرَضْنَا مَعْنَاهُ قَدَّرُنَا وَتَقْدِيرُ الشَّارِعِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَمْنَعَ الزِّيَادَةَ أَوْ يَمْنَعَ النُّقْصَانَ وَالْأَوَّلُ مُنتفٍ ؛ لِأَنَّ الْأَعْلَى غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرٍ فِي الْمَهْرِ إجْمَاعًا فَتَعَيَّنَ الثَّانِي فَيَكُونُ الْأدْنَى مُقَدَّرًا ، وَلَمَّا لَمْ يُبَيِّنُ ذَلِكَ الْمَفْرُوضَ قَدْرُنَاهُ بِطَرِيقِ الرَّأْيِ وَالْقِيَاسِ بِشَيْءٍ هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ شَرُعًا فِي مِثْلٍ هَذَا الْبَابِ أَى : كَوْنُهُ عِوَضًا لِبَعْضِ أَعْضَاءِ الْإِنْسَانِ وَهُوَ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا وُجُوبُ قَطْعِ الْيَدِ ، وَعِندَ الشَّافِعِيِّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كُلُّ مَا يَصْلُحُ ثَمَنًا يَصْلُحُ مَهْرًا
And His saying, exalted be He, 'that you seek with your wealth' — the letter 'ba' is a specific word that necessitates attachment, so the seeking (i.e., the valid contract) is not separated from the wealth; thus it is obligatory with the contract itself. Contrary to the invalid (contract), for the dower is not obligatory with the contract itself when it is invalid. Contrary to al-Shafi'i, and the disagreement here is regarding the case of al-mufawwida, i.e., she who marries without dower or marries on the condition that there is no dower for her: the dower is not obligatory according to al-Shafi'i may Allah have mercy on him until death, and most of them (his followers) hold the dower obligatory when he has consummated with her. And according to us, a full dower of the like is obligatory when he has consummated with her or one of them dies. And His saying, exalted be He, 'We have known what We have prescribed for them' (33:38) — He specified the prescription of the dower i.e., its determination by the Lawgiver, so its minimum is determined, contrary to him (al-Shafi'i). Because His word 'faradna' means 'we have determined' and the determination of the Lawgiver either prevents increase or prevents decrease; the first is negated because the maximum is not determined in the dower by consensus, so the second is confirmed, thus the minimum is determined. And since that prescribed (amount) was not explained, we determined it by way of opinion and analogy with something that is legally considered in such a chapter, i.e., its being a compensation for some parts of a human: it is ten dirhams, for the obligation of cutting off the hand is attached to them. And according to al-Shafi'i may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him, everything valid as a price is valid as a dower.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of mahr (dower) in marriage, deriving the obligation and minimum value from Quranic texts and qiyas (analogy). The author first addresses verse 4:24 'an tabtaghu bi-amwalikum', focusing on the letter 'ba' which indicates attachment (ilṣāq). The argument is that since the 'ba' attaches the seeking (i.e., the marriage contract) to wealth (mahr), the mahr becomes obligatory immediately upon the contract itself in a valid marriage. This is contradicted by Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that in a tafwid marriage (where no mahr is specified), mahr is not obligatory until death or consummation. The Hanafi position is that mahr is wajib from the contract, though payment may be deferred. The passage then moves to verse 33:38 'qad 'alimna ma faradna 'alayhim', interpreting 'faradna' as 'we have determined' (taqdir). Since the Lawgiver determined the mahr, it implies a minimum limit; otherwise determination would be meaningless. The maximum is left open by consensus, so the minimum must be fixed. As the Quran does not specify the amount, the author uses qiyas: comparing mahr to the minimum value for stealing (nisaab) which triggers hand-cutting (10 dirhams), since both involve compensation. Thus the minimum mahr is set at ten dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, allowing any valid price as mahr. The commentary follows the author's order: proof from verse 4:24, then the dispute, then the proof from verse 33:38 and qiyas.

Key Terms
فرض (faraḍa): To determine or prescribe; in the verse, it means the Lawgiver set a limit.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Dower of the like, used when no dower is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum mahr in Hanafi fiqh as derived from qiyas?
A) 5 dirhams.
B) 10 dirhams.
C) 20 dirhams.
D) No fixed minimum.

Key Takeaway
The minimum mahr of 10 dirhams is derived from Quran 33:38's implication of a fixed minimum and qiyas on the theft nisab.

Deriving Mahr Obligation from the Khas in Quran 4:24
Quranic derivation of mahr obligation at contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of khas (specification) to derive the ruling that mahr is wajib at the moment of a valid marriage contract, and evaluate the Shafi'i alternative reading.

Core Idea
The ba' al-ilsaq attaches mahr to the contract, making it wajib at the moment of the marriage contract, not later.

This passage demonstrates how a single letter (ba') in a Quranic verse can determine a major fiqh ruling. It also shows the Hanafi methodology of deriving rulings by identifying a khas (specific) textual element and applying its linguistic function. Understanding this derivation is critical for grasping the Hanafi position on mahr and the usul principle of takhsis al-khas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disputed ruling
Understand the case of a woman (mufawwidah) marrying without specifying mahr. The dispute is whether mahr becomes obligatory at the contract or later.
The Hanafi position: mahr is wajib at the contract. Shafi'i: mahr is due upon death or consummation.
2
Locate the Quranic proof and the operative word
Examine Quran 4:24, specifically the phrase 'biamwalikum'. The preposition ba' is the key element; it is considered khas (specific) in Hanafi usul, indicating ilsaq (attachment).
The verse: 'Wa uhillu lakum ma wara'a dhalikum an tabtaghu biamwalikum.'
3
Classify the ba' linguistically
In Hanafi usul, the ba' in 'biamwalikum' is classified as a khas, specifically ba' al-ilsaq. This means it attaches what follows (wealth/mahr) to what precedes (seeking marriage/the contract).
This classification is decisive for the derivation.
4
Apply the function to derive the ruling
Attachment implies that mahr is linked to the act of seeking marriage (ibtigha'), which refers to the valid marriage contract. Therefore, mahr becomes obligatory at the moment of the contract, not upon later events.
The obligation is immediate, though payment is deferred to consummation or death.
5
Distinguish valid from fasid marriage
The term 'ibtigha' is restricted to valid (sahih) marriage. In a fasid (invalid) marriage, the same derivation does not apply; mahr becomes wajib only upon consummation or death.
This is a taqyid (restriction) of the general ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاص کے حکم پر تیسری تفریح تشریح ان تبتغوا: ۔ یہاں سے ماتین علیہ الرحمہ خاص کے حکم پر تیسری تفریح ذکر فرمار ہے ہیں اس تفریح سے پہلے مسئلہ سمجھیں کہ مفوضہ عورت یعنی وہ عورت جو خود کسی سے نکاح کرے یا اس کا ولی اس کا نکاح کرائے اور یہ شرط لگا ئیں کہ مہر نہیں ہوگا یا بغیر مہر کے ذکر کے نکاح ہوا تو خاوند پر مہر کب فرض ہوگا ؟ اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ نفس عقد کے ساتھ مہر لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ جب وہ خاوند مرے گا تو اس پر مہر لازم ہو جائے گا اور اکثر اصحاب شوافع یہ کہتے ہیں کہ جب خاوند دخول کرے گا اس وقت مہر لازم ہو گا اس سے پہلے لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن احناف کے ہاں مہر کا وجوب نفس عقد سے ہی ہو جائے گا ہاں ادائیگی اس وقت واجب ہوگی جب دخول ہوگا یا ان میں سے کوئی ایک مرجائے گا۔ دلیل:۔ احناف کی دلیل جو خاس کے حکم پر تفریح بھی ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے واصل لکم ماوراء ذالکم ان تبغوا باموالکم یہاں مال کے ساتھ عورتوں سے نکاح کرنے کو حلال قرار دیا گیا ہے اور یہاں باموالکم“ پر ”ب“ خاص ہے اس کا موجب الصاق ہوتا ہے یعنی یہ اپنے مابعد کو ماقبل کے ساتھ ملا دیتی ہے اور آیت میں ماقبل ہے ابتغاء یعنی طلب اور اس سے مراد نکاح صحیح ہے تو ”ب“ کے موجب کے مطابق مال کا نکاح کے ساتھ ملا ہوا ہونا ضروری ہے تو اس آیت سے ثابت ہوا کہ مال (مہر ) نفس عقد سے ہی لازم ہو جاتا ہے اگر نفس عقد سے واجب نہ ہو تو خاص "ب" کے موجب پر عمل نہیں ہوگا البتہ اگر نکاح فاسد ہو تو پھر نفس عقد سے مہر واجب نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں ابتغاء سے مراد نکاح صحیح ہے۔ نکاح فاسد یہاں مراد نہیں ہے اس لیے نکاح فاسد میں اس وقت مہر واجب ہوگا جب دخول کرے گا یا مر جائے گا۔
Third Tafri'ah on the Ruling of Khas: Explanation of 'in tabtaghu': From here, the author, may Allah have mercy on him, mentions the third tafri'ah on the ruling of khas. Before this tafri'ah, understand the issue: For a mufawwidah woman (i.e., a woman who marries herself or her guardian marries her with the condition that there is no mahr, or a marriage without mentioning mahr), when does mahr become obligatory on the husband? There is disagreement. Imam al-Shafi'i says that mahr is not binding at the very contract, but rather when the husband dies, then mahr becomes binding. And most of the Shafi'i companions say that mahr becomes binding when the husband consummates the marriage; before that it is not binding. But according to the Hanafis, the obligation of mahr occurs at the very contract itself—yes, payment becomes obligatory when consummation occurs or when one of them dies. Proof: The Hanafi proof, which is also a tafri'ah on the ruling of khas, is that in the Holy Quran it is said: 'Wa uhillu lakum ma wara'a dhalikum an tabtaghu biamwalikum' (Lawful to you are what is beyond that, that you seek [marriage] with your wealth). Here, marriage with women is made lawful with wealth, and the 'ba' in 'biamwalikum' is specific (khas). Its function is to connect (ilsaq), i.e., it attaches what comes after to what comes before. In the verse, what comes before is 'ibtigha' (seeking), i.e., valid marriage contract. So according to the function of 'ba', it is necessary that wealth is attached to the marriage contract. Thus, from this verse it is proven that wealth (mahr) becomes binding at the very contract. If it were not obligatory at the very contract, then the function of the specific 'ba' would not be acted upon. However, if the marriage is fasid, then mahr is not obligatory at the contract because here 'ibtigha' refers to valid marriage; fasid marriage is not meant here. Therefore, in a fasid marriage, mahr becomes obligatory when consummation occurs or one of them dies.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is an istinbat (derivation) of the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of mahr at the moment of a valid marriage contract. It begins by introducing the third tafri'ah (sub-branch) on the ruling of khas, specifically applied to the issue of mahr. The author first clarifies the scenario: a woman who marries without specifying mahr or with a condition of no mahr. The Shafi'i school, in two opinions, holds that mahr is not due at the contract but only upon death (as per Shafi'i himself) or upon consummation (as per his followers). The Hanafi position is that mahr becomes wajib (obligatory) at the very moment of the valid contract, although payment (ada') is deferred to consummation or death. The proof is based on the Quranic verse (4:24) which uses 'bi amwalikum' with the letter ba' al-ilsaq. In Hanafi usul, the ba' of ilsaq indicates attachment, so the mahr (wealth) must be attached to the seeking of marriage (the contract). Thus, the ruling that mahr is due at the contract is derived. However, this applies only to valid (sahih) marriage; in a fasid marriage, the contract is not a valid 'ibtigha', so mahr is not due at the contract but only upon consummation or death. This is a clear example of applying the usul principle of khas to a fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
خاص (khas): A specific term or letter that restricts the general meaning; here, the ba' in 'biamwalikum' is considered khas indicating attachment.
مہر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife in marriage; its obligation arises at the contract in Hanafi fiqh.
باء الصاق (ba' al-ilsaq): A specific preposition that attaches one thing to another; in this verse, it attaches the wealth to the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proof from the Quranic verse (4:24), what does the ba' (ب) in 'biamwalikum' indicate about the timing of mahr obligation?
A) Mahr is due only upon consummation.
B) Mahr is due upon the death of the husband.
C) Mahr is due at the moment of the valid marriage contract.
D) Mahr is due only if specified at the contract.

Key Takeaway
The ba' al-ilsaq in the Quranic verse proves that mahr is wajib at the moment of a valid marriage contract in Hanafi fiqh.

Deriving Rulings from General and Specific Texts: The Theft Verse Liability Dispute
Urdu commentary on applying 'amm and khass to theft verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a specific text (khass) can be qualified by another textual indication to derive the ruling on liability in theft, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school negates liability in theft because the punishment is attributed to Allah, not the servant.

This lesson explores a nuanced usul argument from a Hanafi commentary on the theft verse. The commentator defends the position that no financial liability (daman) is incurred alongside the hadd penalty, using the phrase 'jaza'an bima kasaba nakalan min Allah' as a proof. We will walk through the logical steps that the Hanafi school employs to derive this ruling and contrast it with the Shafi'i perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and the Hanafi claim
Recognize that the objector asserts the Hanafi school is ignoring the specific command 'cut off their hands' by denying liability. The commentator clarifies they do not rely on that verse for this ruling.
The objection is based on the principle that a specific text (khass) must be acted upon according to its apparent meaning.
2
Locate the alternative proof
Find the phrase 'jaza'an bima kasaba nakalan min Allah' (Al-Ma'idah 5:38) which the Hanafi school uses as the primary evidence.
This phrase is operative because it attributes the punishment directly to Allah.
3
Analyze the attribution to Allah
Understand the Hanafi reasoning: since the punishment is 'from Allah', it indicates the transgression is against Allah's right. For that to hold, the stolen property must be in Allah's sanctity, which means it leaves the servant's sanctity.
This step involves a logical inference (qiyas) based on the concept of 'ismah (sanctity).
4
Derive the ruling and contrast with opposing school
Conclude that only the hand-cutting penalty applies, not liability. Compare with the Shafi'i position that requires both hadd and restitution because they read the verse as a whole.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is clear: in Hanafi fiqh, the thief does not return the stolen item after punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے جدا کرنے پر ۔ یہاں اس بات کا تذکرہ نہیں ہے کہ مال بندے کی عصمت سے نکل جاتا ہے یا نہی ؟ اسی طرح مال کی ضمان آئے گی یا نہیں؟ تو جب اس بات کا یہاں کوئی تذکرہ نہیں ہے تو اس بات کو لیا جائے اور کہا جائے کہ چوری کے وقت مال بندے کی عصمت سے نکل جاتا ہے۔ اس لیے ضمان نہیں آئے گی تو خاص کے معنی پر عمل نہیں ہوگا حالانکہ خاص اپنے معنی میں قطعا حکم کو ثابت کرتا ہے۔
جواب:۔ آپ کا اعتراض اس صورت میں درست تھا کہ ہم ضمان کے لازم نہ ہونے پر فاقطعوا اید یہما سے دلیل پکڑتے ہوں اور خاص کے معنی پر عمل نہ کرتے ہوں حالانکہ ہم اس سے دلیل نہیں پکڑتے بلکہ ہم اپنی بات کو اللہ تعالٰی کے اس فرمان سے ثابت کرتے ہیں۔ کہ " جزاء بما کسبا نکالا من اللہ یہاں جزا کی نسبت اللہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے اور جس جزا کی نسبت اللہ کی طرف ہو وہ اللہ کے حق میں جنایت کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے نہ کہ بندے کے حق میں جنایت کی وجہ سے تو گویا یہاں چوری پر جو عقوبت ہو رہی ہے وہ اللہ کے حق میں جنایت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہورہی ہے اور اللہ کے حق میں جنایت کے صحیح ہونے کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ جس مال کو چوری کیا گیا ہے وہ اللہ کی عصمت میں ہو تبھی تو اس میں اللہ کا حق ثابت ہوگا تو جب مال اللہ کی عصمت میں جائے گا تو لا زمادہ بندے کی عصمت سے نکل جائے گا۔ تو بندے کی عصمت سے نکلنے والا معنی ہم نے جزاء بما كسبا نکالا من الله " سے ثابت کیا ہے نہ کہ فاقطعوا ایدہما سے کہ ہم پر اعتراض لازم آئے کہ آپ نے خاص کے معنی پر عمل نہیں کیا۔ تو جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ چوری کے وقت مال اللہ کی عصمت میں ہوتا ہے اور اس پر عقوبت اللہ کے حق میں جنایت کی وجہ سے ہے۔ تو یہ عقوبت صرف قطع ید سے ہو گی ۔ ضمان لازم نہیں آئے گی کیونکہ ضمان کا محتاج بندہ ہے۔ اس لیے ضمان بندے کے حق میں جنایت کی وجہ سے لازم آتا ہے۔
Regarding separation. Here there is no mention of whether the property leaves the sanctity of the servant or not. Similarly, whether liability (daman) will be incurred or not. So when there is no mention of this here, this matter is taken and it is said that at the time of theft, the property leaves the sanctity of the servant. Therefore, liability is not incurred. Thus, the meaning of the specific (khass) would not be acted upon, even though the specific in its meaning definitively establishes the ruling. Answer: Your objection would have been correct if we were holding proof from 'faqta'u aidiyahuma' for the non-necessity of liability and not acting upon the meaning of the specific, whereas we do not hold proof from it. Rather, we establish our statement from the command of Allah Most High: 'jaza'an bima kasaba nakalan min Allah.' Here, the recompense is attributed to Allah, and whatever recompense is attributed to Allah is due to transgression against the right of Allah, not due to transgression against the right of the servant. So it is as if the punishment for theft here is due to transgression against the right of Allah. For the validity of transgression against Allah's right, it is necessary that the property stolen is in the sanctity of Allah, only then Allah's right is established. So when the property enters Allah's sanctity, it necessarily leaves the servant's sanctity. So the meaning of leaving the servant's sanctity we have established from 'jaza'an bima kasaba nakalan min Allah', not from 'faqta'u aidiyahuma', so that the objection would apply that you did not act upon the meaning of the specific. So when it is established that at the time of theft the property is in Allah's sanctity and the punishment for it is due to transgression against Allah's right, then this punishment will only be cutting of the hand. Liability will not be incurred because liability requires the servant. Therefore, liability is incurred due to transgression against the servant's right.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) addressing an objection regarding the application of general ('amm) and specific (khass) in the theft verse. The objector claimed that if one argues from the general command 'cut off their hands' (al-Ma'idah 5:38) that liability (daman) does not apply, that would contradict acting upon the specific meaning of the verse. The commentator (implicitly the author of the sharh) responds that they do not rely on that verse for the negation of liability; rather, they use the verse 'jaza'an bima kasaba nakalan min Allah' (al-Ma'idah 5:38) which attributes the punishment to Allah, indicating that the punishment is for transgressing Allah's right. For that to be valid, the stolen property must be in Allah's sanctity, which means it leaves the servant's sanctity. Thus, the specific meaning of 'cut off their hands' is not being neglected; rather, the ruling is derived from another proof. The commentary then concludes that the punishment is only cutting of the hand, not liability, because liability is for the right of the servant. This illustrates the usul principle that a general text can be qualified by other evidence, and that acting upon a specific ruling does not require ignoring another specific ruling if they are based on different aspects.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A specific ruling or text that applies to a particular category, here the command to cut hands.
عام ('amm): A general term that encompasses all individuals of its category, here the phrase 'the thief' or 'cut off their hands'.
عصمت ('ismah): Sanctity or inviolability; the protection given to property by Allah's right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, why is liability (daman) not required in addition to cutting of the hand for theft?
A) Because the verse 'cut off their hands' is general and excludes liability.
B) Because the punishment is attributed to Allah, indicating it is for His right, not the servant's.
C) Because the thief is poor and cannot pay.
D) Because liability is only for murder, not theft.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the attribution of punishment to Allah in the theft verse serves as the basis for excluding liability, demonstrating that a specific text (khass) can be qualified by another textual indication.

intermediate
6 min
Nakira Mawsufa: The Rule of Indefinite Noun with General Adjective
Rule: indefinite noun with general adjective becomes general, with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that an indefinite noun qualified by a general adjective indicates generality, and explain the reasoning using the Quranic proof from Surah al-Baqara 2:221.

Core Idea
Indefinite noun + general adjective = general meaning, as proven by the ta'lil in Quran 2:221.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the construction of an indefinite noun (nakira) followed by a general adjective (sifa 'amma) is a key indicator of generality. This lesson unpacks the rule through a linguistic example and a powerful Quranic proof from Surah al-Baqara, demonstrating how understanding this principle affects legal rulings derived from such texts.

Guided Path
1
Define the rule
State the rule: an indefinite noun described by a general adjective becomes general in meaning.
This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul.
2
Apply to ordinary language example
Consider the phrase 'I will not sit except with a learned man'. Identify 'rajulan' as indefinite and 'aliman' as a general adjective, making the noun general.
The example shows practical application in everyday speech.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Analyze Quran 2:221: 'And a believing slave is better than an idolater'. Identify 'abdun' as indefinite and 'mu'minun' as a general adjective.
The verse is used as a dalil for the rule.
4
Understand the ta'lil reasoning
The verse serves as a rationale (ta'lil) for the preceding general command prohibiting marriage with idolaters. Since the command is general, the rationale must also be general, confirming the generality of 'abdun mu'minun'.
This reasoning is key to the Hanafi position.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Conclude that an indefinite noun with a general adjective indicates generality, and this is reinforced by contextual factors like ta'lil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نکرہ موصوفہ بصفتہ عامتہ کا حکم اور دلائل

وكذ النكرة الموصوفة بصفة عامه: وہ نکرہ جو موصوف ہو کسی صفت کے ساتھ اور وہ صفت عام ہو تو یہ نکرہ بھی عام ہوگا جیسے کوئی کہے ”لا اجالس الارجلا عالما " یہاں رجلا نمرہ ہے اور اس کی صفت عالما عام ہے اسی وجہ سے رجلا عام ہے تو اب اس آدمی کے لیے ہر عالم کی مجلس میں بیٹھنا جائز ہو گا۔

دلیل اول: لقولہ تعالٰی ولعبد مومن :۔ یہاں سے ماتن اس کرہ کے عام ہونے کی پہلی مثال اور دلیل پیش کرتے ہیں کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ولعبد مومن خیر من مشرک یہاں "عبد" کمرہ ہے اس کی صفت "مومن " عام ہے اسی وجہ سے عہد بھی عام ہے کہ ہر مومن آدمی مشرک سے بہتر ہے۔ اور اس کے عام ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس سے پہلے حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ ولا تنکو المشرکین حتی ایو منوا یہ حکم عام ہے اور ولعبد مومن الابتہ یہ اس حکم کی تعلیل کے طور پر بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ اور کیونکہ حکم عام ہے اس لیے علیت بھی عام ہوگی۔ تو اگر ولعبد مومن کو عام نہ مانا جائے تو تعلیل صحیح نہیں ہوگی اس لیے اس کو عام ماننا پڑے گا تو ثابت ہوا
The ruling and proofs of the indefinite noun described by a general adjective. And likewise, the indefinite noun described by a general adjective: the indefinite noun that is qualified by an adjective and that adjective is general, then this indefinite noun will also be general. For example, if someone says, 'I will not sit except with a learned man' ('لا اجالس الا عالما'). Here 'rajulan' is indefinite, and its adjective 'aliman' is general; for this reason 'rajulan' is general. So now for that man, it becomes permissible to sit with every learned person. First proof: The saying of Allah Most High: 'And a believing slave is better than an idolater' (Quran 2:221). Here 'abdun' is indefinite, its adjective 'mu'minun' is general, so 'abdun' is also general, meaning every believing person is better than an idolater. And the proof of its generality is that before this, a command was given: 'Do not marry idolaters until they believe' (Quran 2:221). This command is general, and the verse 'And a believing slave...' was revealed as an explanation of the rationale for this command. And since the command is general, the rationale must also be general. So if 'And a believing slave' is not taken as general, the rationale would not be correct. Therefore it must be taken as general; thus it is proven.
Source pages p. 615

Commentary
This passage presents another usul rule: an indefinite noun (nakira) that is described by a general adjective (sifa 'amma) becomes general, encompassing all individuals possessing that attribute. The commentator expands on the matn with examples and Quranic proof. The example given is 'I will not sit except with a learned man' – here 'a man' is general because 'learned' is a general description; thus it includes all learned men. The Quranic proof is from Surah al-Baqara (2:221): 'And a believing slave is better than an idolater.' The word 'abdun (slave) is nakira, described by 'mu'minun' (believing), which is general. The verse comes after the prohibition of marrying idolaters, serving as a rationale (ta'lil). Since the prohibition is general over all idolaters, the rationale must also be general, meaning every believing person (male or female slave or free) is better than any idolater. Thus the nakira with a general adjective indicates generality. This principle is used in Hanafi usul to derive rulings from such constructions.

Key Terms
نکرہ موصوفہ بصفتہ عامتہ (nakira mawsufa bi-sifati-ha al-'amma): An indefinite noun that is qualified by a general adjective, making the noun general.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the phrase 'a believing slave' in Quran 2:221 considered general?
A) Because 'slave' is a general term covering all slaves.
B) Because it is used as a rationale for a general command.
C) Because the word 'better' implies a comparison.
D) Because it is a direct command from Allah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an indefinite noun qualified by a general adjective indicates generality, as demonstrated by the Quranic rationale in Surah al-Baqara 2:221.
